Northwest Joint Transportation Completed

Old Kiln Permanent Wharf Completed, China Merchants Hai Rui to Dock Today 128

The old kiln wharf in Lianyungang will be fully completed in the spring of next year. A portion has already been completed and named "Permanent". Merchant ships will begin docking today. Details are as follows:

Newly Built Wharf In the past, ships traveling to the old kiln unloaded passengers and cargo at Sunjia Mountain, using barges, which was costly and time-consuming. The new wharf in Lianyungang, extending into the sea along the breakwater, is nearing completion. It can accommodate three ships at the same time when fully completed. The completed portion can accommodate one ship for now. The Longhai Railway has notified the China Merchants Bureau that the Hai Rui ship, arriving at the kiln today (the 4th), will begin docking at the "Permanent" wharf for loading and unloading. The Railway Bureau and the China Merchants Bureau's Haizhou branch have specially invited local customers to visit the new wharf today and provide refreshments.

Saving Time The waves in Liantan Port are extremely large, and the work of cargo ships is often delayed by the waves, sometimes taking three or four days to load a single cargo, resulting in huge losses. After the completion of the new Permanent wharf, the waves will be blocked by the breakwater. When fully completed next spring, three ships can dock at the same time, and they can be unloaded as soon as they arrive, without hindrance, reducing the time for ships to stop, which is of great importance to shipping operations.

Seeking to Seize Work There are more than 100 local laborers who are seeking to seize loading and unloading work. In November of last year, there was a conflict. The Longhai Railway dispatched more than 100 armed road protection police to suppress it.

The loading and unloading work was then taken over by the railway police. Now that a portion of the wharf has been completed and ships can dock, the laborers in Haizhou, for the sake of their livelihood, are seeking to seize the loading and unloading work, and the situation is very tense.

Water and Land Precautions After the news spread, the Longhai Railway authorities, fearing a disturbance when the ship docks at the wharf today, have transferred 150 armed police from the road protection team from Zhengzhou to the Permanent New Wharf to be on guard. When the China Merchants Bureau's Hai Rui ship traveled from Shanghai to Haizhou, fearing that the laborers would board the ship and forcibly seize the waterfront work, it requested the head office to send six additional armed escorts to accompany the ship to the old kiln for precaution. The Railway Bureau has also prepared an armored train to suppress the situation at the old kiln. Therefore, both the railway and shipping companies hope that no disturbance will occur when the ship docks at the new wharf today.

Tax Affairs Department Advises Compliance

Shipping Association Will Reconvene to Discuss the Tariff Notice of the Pilotage Committee 129

According to the New New Society, after the implementation of the newly revised Provisional Rules for Song-Han Pilotage by the Shanghai Pilotage Administration Committee, the Shipping Association believed that the tax rates had increased significantly and the shipping industry could not afford the burden. In addition to sending telegrams to the Yuan and Ministry to appeal against it, it also planned to suspend navigation in unison if necessary to show its determination. It is learned that Robert de Keyserlingk, Commissioner of Customs of the Jianghai Customs, specially advised the shipping companies to comply yesterday. It is said that the shipping companies will reconvene to discuss. The details are as follows:

(Advise Compliance) The Shipping Association believes that the new pilotage fee rate is more than double the previous rate, so it specially convened a meeting and unanimously decided that if the customs refuses to close the customs due to the pilotage issue, all non-scheduled ships that hire pilots for short-term trips to the Yangtze River will suspend navigation. It is learned that Robert de Keyserlingk, Commissioner of Customs of the Jianghai Customs, believes that the suspension of ships will inevitably affect traffic and is of great importance. Although the new pilotage fee rate of the Song-Han District Pilotage Administration Committee has increased compared to the past, the previous pilotage fee seemed to be too low, so he advised Yu Qiaqing, Chairman of the Shipping Association, Yuan Ludeng, and other members yesterday to explain it to the shipping companies and comply with the newly revised pilotage rules. It is heard that the Shipping Association believes that this matter is of great importance to the future of the shipping companies and plans to convene another meeting for final discussion.

(Notice of Charges) Karel, Chairman of the Shanghai Pilotage Administration Committee, sent letters to various shipping companies yesterday, notifying them that all pilotage fees should be collected by the accountant of the association on a regular basis from this month onwards. The original letter is recorded as follows: Sirs, this association intends to implement full management of short-term pilots, that is, pilots who have not been employed by various Yangtze River shipping companies on a long-term basis, from October 1st. After October 1st, the pilotage fees should be calculated according to the attached pilotage fee rates and a copy of the Provisional Rules for Pilotage Administration is also attached. Please pay special attention to Articles 13 and 14 of these rules. In the future, pilots must be dispatched by the Song-Han District Pilotage Office. If you need to use them, please contact the office in the Maritime Affairs Patrol Office on the fourth floor of the Jianghai Customs, so that you will not be mistaken. All pilotage fees should be collected by the accountant of this association on a regular basis and should not be paid to individual pilots. This is very important. I am sending this letter to you and hope you will check it.

Provisional Rules Article 1 of the Provisional Rules for Song-Han District Pilotage: These Provisional Rules are promulgated in accordance with Article 3 of the Provisional Regulations on Pilotage Administration Article 3: The agency for managing pilotage affairs is in accordance with the provisions of Article 1, Chapter 1 of the Provisional Regulations on Pilotage Administration Article 3: In accordance with the rules of Article 2, Chapter 1 of the Provisional Regulations on Pilotage Administration, the Shanghai Pilotage Administration Committee's two representatives from the Ministry of Finance designate the Maritime Affairs Patrol Officer and the Harbor Master, with the Maritime Affairs Patrol Officer as the chairman and the Harbor Master as the executive member. Article 4: The Song-Han Pilotage District starts from the Wusong Sanjia Water Lighthouse and ends at the Xianghekou in Hankou, Hubei. Article 5: The number of pilots and pilot trainees shall be allocated by the Management Committee at any time according to the needs of the shipping industry. Article 6: Pilots are divided into the following three classes: Class A pilots, Class B pilots, Class C pilots, and short-term pilots, piloting ships without fixed schedules on the Yangtze River, such as ships sailing in the ocean and along the coast; Long-term pilots, piloting ships with fixed schedules on the Yangtze River, such as river ships and shallow-water ships and small warships; Ships with a draft of 18 feet or more are only allowed to use Class A pilots; Ships with a draft of 18 feet or less and 15 feet or more can use Class A and Class B pilots; Ships with a draft of 15 feet or less can use Class A, Class B, and Class C pilots; Pilots who are employed on a long-term basis to pilot river ships, shallow-water ships, small warships, etc., commonly known as long-term pilots, usually receive a fixed monthly salary and are part of the crew. Class A, Class B, and Class C pilots can all serve, but they can only receive the salary of ordinary river ship pilots and cannot collect fees according to the pilotage fee rates. Article 12: All pilots, standby pilots, and pilot trainees shall obey the lawful orders of the manager. The manager has the right to suspend pilots who disobey first and wait for the Harbor Master to handle it, and has the right to execute other disciplinary actions assigned by the Management Committee. Pilots who disagree with the manager's decision may appeal to the Harbor Master. Article 13: All pilots, standby pilots, and pilot trainees must abide by the rules stipulated in the Provisional Regulations on Pilotage Administration, and Chapter 4, from Article 20 to Article 30, should be carried out especially. Article 14: In order to facilitate the handling of pilotage affairs, the Song-Han District Pilotage Office is specially established in Shanghai. The Pilotage Administration Committee appoints a manager to manage its affairs. The manager is subordinate to the Harbor Master, who is the executive member of the Management Committee, and is directly responsible to him. All pilots and office staff should have due respect for the manager. Article 15: The manager's main responsibilities are as follows: A. Dispatching pilots to board ships for service in accordance with the regulations and rules; B. Supervising the registration, accounting, and safekeeping of files in the office; C. At the end of each month, a report on the expenses of the office shall be prepared and submitted to the Harbor Master for forwarding to the Pilotage Administration Committee; D. Executing the instructions issued by the Harbor Master. Article 16: The office hours of the office are from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM in the morning and from 1:30 PM to 5:00 PM in the afternoon. On Saturdays, it is from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM in the morning and on Sundays, it is from 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM. The office hours on holidays are handled in accordance with the customs regulations. Article 17: Each pilot on duty on the duty roster shall not leave without authorization unless instructed and shall be in close proximity to the office. He shall report to the office from 4:00 PM to 5:00 PM every day. Article 18: If a pilot is unable to go to the office in person due to illness, he shall report it in writing or by telephone. If the illness extends beyond 48 hours, a certificate should be issued by a doctor approved by the Management Committee. Article 19: Pilots shall not leave their posts without the consent of the manager, except for illness, and shall not be on duty. If there are any of the above circumstances, disciplinary action may be taken. Article 20: When a pilot is dispatched to serve and returns to port after completing the task, he shall submit a report to the manager in the prescribed form, stating the details of the ship he led and the amount of pilotage fee he received. Article 21: Pilotage fees shall be collected by the accountant of the Committee in accordance with the fee rates determined by the Management Committee from time to time. Pilots shall not collect pilotage fees from the ships they led without authorization. Pilots who violate this article may be subject to disciplinary action. Article 22: The fee rate calculated by tonnage shall be based on its registered tonnage. Ships that have not been measured and registered by tonnage, such as warships, etc., shall be calculated by converting three tons of displacement into one registered ton. Article 23: The fee rate calculated by draft shall be based on the minimum draft of ten feet. When calculating pilotage fees, any fraction less than one foot shall also be counted as one foot. Article 24: If a ship with a very shallow draft is encountered, the fee may be less than the fixed rate and may be temporarily determined and collected by the Harbor Master on behalf of the Management Committee. Article 25: When shifting ships in the northern ports along the river, whether it is lowering anchor or raising anchor, or berthing or leaving the dock, a fee of one yuan per mile per foot of draft shall be charged. Any odd numbers less than one mile and one foot shall also be counted as one mile and one foot. Article 26: A. Pilots dispatched to Wusong to wait for ships, regardless of whether the ship arrives in Wusong or not, shall be charged a detention fee of ten yuan for every 12 hours from the time they are instructed to be in Wusong; B. If a ship stops at an intermediate port or loads or unloads cargo at another port, a detention fee of ten yuan shall be charged for every 24 hours or less than 24 hours; C. If a ship loads and unloads cargo in port and no longer needs a pilot, the pilot shall be provided with the cost of a second-class ticket for a ship or train to or from Shanghai, and from the time the pilot is dismissed until the ship arrives in Shanghai, or from the time the ship departs from Shanghai until the ship leaves the port, a fee of ten yuan shall be paid for every 24 hours, and if it is less than one day but more than twelve hours, it shall also be counted as one day. In any case, the minimum fee shall be ten yuan; D. The application to dispatch a pilot may be withdrawn, but if the ship is scheduled to leave port on the same day and the pilot has already been dispatched, or if the ship is scheduled to leave port on the next day and the application is withdrawn after 5:00 PM, a withdrawal fee of ten yuan shall be charged. These rules may be amended at any time if necessary. These rules shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

(Pilotage Fee Rates) According to the New Sound Society (Table 1): Calculated by the number of feet of the ship's draft, the pilotage fee per foot of draft or fraction thereof: (A) (At least one Class A pilot must be used) Wusong to or from Tongzhou 2.5 yuan, Zhenjiang 7 yuan, Shi'erxu 8 yuan, Nanjing 9 yuan, Caishiji 10 yuan, Taiping 10.5 yuan, Wuhu 11 yuan, Digang 16 yuan, Jiujiang 18 yuan, Daye 20 yuan, Hankou 22 yuan; (B) Using Class B and Class C pilots, Wusong to or from Tongzhou 2 yuan, Zhenjiang 5 yuan, Shi'erxu 6 yuan, Nanjing 7 yuan, Caishiji 8 yuan, Taiping 8.5 yuan, Wuhu 9 yuan, Digang 10 yuan, Jiujiang 14 yuan, Daye 16 yuan, Hankou 18 yuan. The fee rates for various sections from Nantong to Hankou are omitted. (Table 2) Calculated by tonnage, the fee rate per registered ton is: Wusong to or from Tongzhou 1 cent, Zhenjiang 1.5 cents, Shi'erxu 1.5 cents, Nanjing 2 cents, Caishiji 2 cents, Taiping 2 cents, Wuhu 2 cents, Digang 3 cents, Jiujiang 3 cents, Daye 3.5 cents, Hankou 4 cents.

(Explanation of Fee Rates) The method of calculating the pilotage fee for Chinese pilots in the Song-Han area is as follows: (1) According to Table 1, multiply the number of feet of draft by the number of silver dollars per foot, and then multiply the registered tonnage by the number of cents of silver dollars per ton according to Table 2. After adding the two products, give a 25% discount (this discount is a temporary measure). For example, if the draft is 19 feet 6 inches and the registered tonnage is 3,400 tons, 19 feet 6 inches should be counted as 20 feet. Looking up Table 1, the fee is 16 yuan per foot, and the product is 320 yuan. The registered tonnage is 3,400 tons. Looking up Table 2, the fee is 3 cents per ton, and the product is 102 yuan. Adding the two products together gives a total of 422 yuan. Giving a 25% discount gives 316 yuan 50 cents. (2) One pilot is allowed to be used to or from Wusong and Wuhu. (3) Two pilots must be used to or from Wusong and ports above Wuhu. No additional fee is currently charged for this additional second pilot. (4) Ships with a draft of more than 18 feet should be calculated according to the Class A fee rate. (5) The fee rate for ships with a draft of less than 18 feet should be determined by the class of pilot used during the period.

Bengbu Salt Crisis Successfully Resolved, Salt Inspector Returns to Shanghai, Four Measures Agreed Upon, Salt Merchants Express Satisfaction 134

According to the Dagong News Agency, the Salt Inspectorate of the Ministry of Finance in this city, due to a dispute between Bengbu salt merchants and the banking community over loan matters, caused a serious crisis in the salt region. Considering that the matter concerned the salt administration, a special commissioner was dispatched to mediate and the matter has been successfully resolved. Commissioner Lu Siding returned to Shanghai yesterday. The details are recorded as follows:

Commissioner Returns to Shanghai: According to Secretary Shen of the Salt Inspectorate of the Ministry of Finance, Bengbu's salt industry has developed considerably in recent years. The four major banks in Shanghai—Bank of China, Shanghai Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, and Jiangsu Bank—considering that the management of salt production in northern Anhui was effective and investment was relatively secure, competed to grant loans. Later, disputes arose between the banks and salt merchants over interest rates and conditions, leading to the stagnation of the salt industry, which greatly affected tax revenue. Therefore, the headquarters specially dispatched Deputy Director Lu Siding and Manager Jin Xiangsheng of the Yangzhou branch to mediate, and a satisfactory resolution has been achieved. Mr. Lu and others returned to the office yesterday to report.

Resolution Measures: The resolution measures are generally agreed upon in four items: (1) Salt that has already been taxed will be allowed for merchants to sell in rotation, to avoid price-cutting competition that would lead to losses. (2) Salt that has already been taxed at the salt yard but has not yet been transported must be completely transported and sold by the end of October. The rotational sales method will continue until the end of December this year, and new taxed salt will be released from January 1 next year. (3) Salt prices will be determined by the merchants themselves, but should not be too high, so that salt that has already been taxed can be sold as soon as possible. (4) The original plan was to release new taxed salt transported from Xiba River to Bengbu at the beginning of November, but the salt merchants requested a delay. The transportation envoy agreed to reconsider at that time. It is reported that the salt merchants are quite satisfied with the above measures, and the past estrangement between officials and merchants has been completely eliminated.

All unpaid field taxes under this item will be subject to a late fee of two-tenths of the tax amount from October 1 to November 30. If the deadline is still exceeded, an additional one-tenth will be added to indicate a penalty. Dangerous Reef Discovered in the Min River

Named Chen Shi Reef, Notice to Navigating Vessels to Pay Attention 138

The Qingyun survey ship of the Navy Department reported that a reef has been discovered in the Min River near the north direction of Min'an Gate, at a distance of 1.52 nautical miles at 193.5 degrees due north of the new Jiyi angle marker, that is, at longitude 119 degrees 31 minutes east and latitude 26 degrees 4 minutes north. The depth of the water is 24 English feet. The reef is a dangerous reef and has been approved by the Navy Department to be named Chen Shi Reef. It will now be included in the nautical chart. Special Notice No. 125 is hereby issued to notify all merchant ships navigating to Fuzhou, ordering them to pay special attention to prevent accidents.

Ye Fenghu Talks About the Drought Situation in Hangzhou County

The Estimated Relief Funds Required Are Over 790,000, Excluding Warehouse Offsets, There Is a Shortfall of Over 600,000 139

The drought in Zhejiang Province this year is the worst in the country, especially in the Hangzhou and Haining area. Ye Fenghu, the magistrate of Hangzhou County, came to Shanghai to beg for donations from various charitable organizations. A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency met him at his lodging yesterday, and he presented a written overview of the disaster situation. The details are recorded as follows:

Affected Land Area: Ye said first that the total area of the county is 1,403,106 mu. The land not affected by the drought or not affected includes fruit, mulberry, tea, cotton, residential, forest, miscellaneous, and public land, as well as water ponds, totaling 773,637 mu. The affected land includes rice paddies, vegetables, hemp, miscellaneous grain farms, and fish, water chestnut, and lotus root ponds, totaling 629,469 mu. The degree of damage is as follows: (1) Rice paddies (A) 20% unsown, (B) 10% sown but no rice harvested, (C) 30% no harvest at all, (D) 70% sown with some harvest, (E) Estimated harvest of 60% for those sown, (F) Average harvest of 42% for those unsown; (2) Vegetables 30%; (3) Hemp land 10%; (4) Miscellaneous grain land 30%; (5) Farms 70%; (6) Other agricultural land 30%; (7) Fish ponds 40%; (8) Water chestnut ponds 50%; (9) Lotus root ponds 60%.

Affected Population: The total population of the county is 393,945, including 134,094 adults, 82,576 elderly (over 41 years old), and 177,275 young people (under 20 years old). (1) 104,736 people do not need relief; (2) 338 people need relief, including 186 unemployed and 152 without occupation; (3) 288,871 people need relief based on their individual disaster situations, including 10,296 workers and 278,575 farmers.

Relief Measures: (1) Relief principles: providing work-for-relief for strong men and giving handicraft capital to strong women to specify weaving linen, cotton, silk cloth, and bamboo weaving. Setting up warehouses to collateralize and circulate. Setting up nursing homes to accommodate young men. Providing rations to those who stay at home. (2) Relief funds: From January to April, work-for-relief is 30 cents per worker, requiring 596,520 yuan. Handicraft capital is 5 yuan per day, requiring 40,500 yuan. Half a liter of rice is given to men, women, the elderly, and the young every day, requiring 144,000 yuan for four months. Firewood costs 14,400 yuan, totaling 795,420 yuan. Sources of funding: 124,993 yuan from the county warehouse deposit and other deposits, with a shortfall of 670,000 yuan. For this reason, I have come to Shanghai to beg for donations from all sectors, hoping that philanthropists will provide assistance so that 300,000 disaster victims can be spared from starvation, etc.

The first is that the Chinese area wants to increase the registration tax by 25%. The reason for this is that the municipal authorities of this city have no funds for construction (including road construction, etc.), so the Finance Bureau suggested increasing house tax and vehicle tax to make up for it. Therefore, regarding the reason for increasing the vehicle tax, it is said that with the municipal license, it is possible to travel on the highways of five provinces and cities. The current increase of 25%, together with the 10% highway surcharge, has not exceeded the amount levied by the special zone. It is also said that, compared to the roads, a special zone license only allows travel for over 300 kilometers, while a municipal license allows travel for over 2,100 kilometers. According to this suggestion, it is very appropriate to add a 25% registration tax. However, the authorities' reason for increasing the tax is based on a comparison with passenger cars for personal use. Our freight truck industry is unfortunately included in the original tax increase plan by the authorities. On our association's side, because the matter concerns the vital interests of all fellow businesses, we have already sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to forward it to the Municipal Government, requesting that this original plan be amended and that we be excluded from the scope of the tax increase. However, the Municipal Government believes that this original plan has been approved by the central government and refuses to amend it. Our association then sent five representatives to the Municipal Government together with representatives from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to petition, and as a result, it was handed over to the two bureaus in charge of finance and public utilities for review. After the report, after guidance from Zhu Yakui, a representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, and Yuan Hongjun, a representative of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the discussion and resolution of the proposal began. (2) Send representatives to Beijing on a fixed date to petition the central government. (2) Send representatives to the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Public Utilities Bureau to petition. (3) After the petition results, convene another meeting on the 11th to discuss relief measures. Chu Fucheng Discusses Eleutherococcus Again 143

Chu Fucheng's reply to the Shanghai Municipal National Medicine Association states: In response to your letter, I am fully aware of your kind concerns. Your letter states that I paid attention to the Eleutherococcus problem and then took Eleutherococcus, which is putting the cart before the horse. I suffered from phlegm and fluid syndrome as a young man, and was prone to catching colds and coughs. I always treated it with Eleutherococcus steamed with pear soup. Now I easily use simple prescriptions, and every prescription must have Eleutherococcus. This is because I often take Eleutherococcus and then pay attention to the Eleutherococcus problem. The attached six pages of prescriptions are sufficient to prove that this statement is not false. Your letter also states that my illness suddenly caused phlegm blockage and shortness of breath because I removed Peucedanum praeruptorum and Perilla frutescens, not because the pharmacies stopped selling Eleutherococcus. However, the facts are the opposite of your opinion. After the Shanghai market stopped selling it, I bought three doses in Minhang and five doses in Jiaxing, all with Eleutherococcus but without Peucedanum praeruptorum and Perilla frutescens (please check the prescriptions). After taking them all, the illness was completely cured, which shows that the medication that treated my illness was Eleutherococcus, not Peucedanum praeruptorum. As for the statement in "Supplement to Compendium of Materia Medica" that Eleutherococcus has a bitter and cold nature and has the effect of clearing the lungs and resolving phlegm, which is the same as the effect of Peucedanum praeruptorum recorded in the Compendium, so it is recommended that Peucedanum praeruptorum can replace Eleutherococcus, I am just a layman, how dare I comment on whether it is appropriate or not. However, reading the announcement of Fan Wenhu, a Ningbo Chinese medicine practitioner, refuting the mistake of using Peucedanum praeruptorum to replace Eleutherococcus, my friend Zhang Qingshi (a native of Nanxun, currently residing in Shanghai), who is somewhat knowledgeable in medicine, recently received a letter from him, also because he caught a cold and wrote his own prescription. The pharmacy refused to sell Eleutherococcus, so he discussed whether Peucedanum praeruptorum could replace Eleutherococcus, saying in brief, "According to the Compendium of Materia Medica, Eleutherococcus can treat wind diseases. Those who cough due to catching a cold cannot do without this medicine. Peucedanum praeruptorum's function is to clear the lungs, but it cannot treat diseases, and it is too releasing. The elderly with yang deficiency and those with weak bodies are all prohibited from using it. The medicinal properties and effects are obviously different, how can they be compared with Eleutherococcus? The pharmacy's refusal to eat due to choking is already inappropriate, and the doctor's rashly agreeing to it is even more harmful." I also received a letter from Shen Gengdao of the Chinese and Western Medicine Research Society, also stating that the four Chinese medicine academic organizations in Shanghai, regardless of the differences in medicinal effects and the safety of patients, ordered Chinese medicine practitioners to abandon Eleutherococcus uniformly and use Peucedanum praeruptorum instead, and specifically wrote an article opposing it. The main points of his article are: "A detailed examination of the effects of Peucedanum praeruptorum and Eleutherococcus shows that they are absolutely different. Although there are similarities in treating coughs, there are also differences. Peucedanum praeruptorum is suitable for coughs with external symptoms, while Eleutherococcus is suitable for coughs without external symptoms. Strictly speaking, Peucedanum praeruptorum has its indications, and Eleutherococcus has its indications. It is absolutely impossible to abandon Eleutherococcus and use Peucedanum praeruptorum exclusively." This only refers to the differences and similarities between Peucedanum praeruptorum and Eleutherococcus in treating coughs. In addition, Eleutherococcus is always used in surgical prescriptions, but Peucedanum praeruptorum is never used. The "Supplement to Compendium of Materia Medica" states that Eleutherococcus can treat throat obstruction, scrofula, breast carbuncle, dorsal carbuncle, all kinds of waste ulcers, swellings, poisonous sores, sores from metal objects, bleeding, fire sores, and other surgical diseases. Rechecking the "Compendium of Materia Medica" entry for Peucedanum praeruptorum shows that it has no effect on treating various surgical diseases, which is inconsistent with the announcement published by the Chinese medicine organization, citing the text of the Compendium," etc. Are these claims true or false? I would like to ask for your wise judgment. A detailed translation of the main points of your letter reveals that the reason why your association and various academic organizations reject Eleutherococcus is nothing more than fear of rising domestic prices and dumping of foreign goods. Your bitter intentions to maintain domestic goods can be understood. However, the intention is correct, but the method is not. In today's era of scientific prosperity, Chinese medicine can still stand on its own entirely because of hundreds of long-lasting and effective domestic medicines. Now, the leaders of your association, without any academic or health basis, arbitrarily change domestic medicines, causing social figures to doubt them, which is tantamount to destroying the Great Wall. It is appropriate to be criticized by Mr. Shuoguo of the New Medicine, claiming bankruptcy for the Old Medicine (see "Shishi Xinbao" on September 21). Therefore, what you are doing will not only cause the reputation of Chinese medicine to fall from now on, or even be completely eliminated, but also the hundreds of millions of domestic medicines will be cut off along with it. Those who plan for the left are no better than you. The letter requesting the mayor's intervention is partly for the health of society and partly for your own sake. If it is said that Eleutherococcus increases in price and other medicines follow suit, making every prescription unaffordable, how can the sick afford it? It is heard that the Zhejiang Construction Department has restricted the selling price of each catty of Eleutherococcus Cooperative to not exceed 150 yuan. Each prescription uses a maximum of four or five mace of Eleutherococcus, with a value of only a few cents. Each prescription uses ten medicines, costing only a few jiao, how can it reach several yuan? The different prices of medicines today and in the past are already understood. Thirty years ago, American ginseng only cost one or two jiao per tael, but now it has risen to over ten yuan per tael. This is clearly a foreign product, why haven't I heard Mr. Chu start a plan to boycott it, and notify colleagues not to prescribe this medicine? Only for Eleutherococcus produced in Zhejiang, he doesn't hesitate to use the strength of a lion to fight a rabbit, uniting Wuxian and Shaoxing to prevent it from being sold. Considering your original intention to maintain domestic products, isn't this going in the opposite direction? I am a native of Zhejiang and have always made it my duty to support the rural areas. Protecting agricultural products is my unavoidable responsibility. If the Eleutherococcus Cooperative can provide reasonable control and limited price increases, I will definitely give it effective support, not just collude with it. This is a special reply to the Shanghai Municipal National Medicine Association, from Chu Fucheng.

If You Don't Lend, I'll Rob

Acquaintances Are No Different From Bandits 146

Pu Fucheng, a peddler from Changshu, 25 years old, living at No. 25 Renshou Lane, Caishi Road, French Concession, stored 48 yuan earned from business savings in a rattan basket on August 21 of this year to return to his native Changshu. You Fengxiang from Wuxi, 42 years old this year, and You Shengxun, 37 years old this year, are brothers who lost their parents at a young age. They were raised by their aunt and taught to learn business. However, Fengxiang was addicted to opium and spent his time wandering around, neglecting his responsibilities. Recently, he has been living at No. 69 Jingtong Village, Xujiahui Road, in the French Concession, making a living by telling stories. Shengxun engaged in business early and worked hard. The meager assets had already been divided early on, and Fengxiang's share had long been exhausted. Shengxun's share remained untouched and even increased slightly each year. Recently, he established the Sanyou Socks Factory at No. 27 Ruichang Lane, Lan Weiai Road, in the French Concession. His business life can be described as thriving. According to the plaintiff You Shengxun's accusation, his brother held a knife and demanded money. The Criminal Investigation Team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau uncovered a morphine manufacturing facility.

A Large Number of Drugs and Sundries Were Found, and Nine Criminals Were Arrested and Sent to the Bureau for Legal Action 149

Zhang Jinbiao (also known as Zhang Zhongguo), a Ningbo native residing at No. 15 Bulin Lane, Gongguan Road, in the French Concession, colluded with Han Bangjie, a Shaoxing native from No. 3 Langjingyi Lane in the French Concession, and a person nicknamed "Fan Wugui" (name unknown) in September of this year. The three of them jointly rented a three-story Western-style building at No. 21 Binggang Lane, Tianbao Road, Zhabei, and falsely established the Hongkang Soap Factory. In reality, they secretly established a morphine manufacturing facility. The internal organization was large-scale, and all kinds of production equipment were complete. A wooden sign reading "(No Visitors)" was hung at the entrance. They also rented a house at No. 26 Linping Road, Xiangyan Bridge, near the facility, and established the Hongkang Soap Factory Distribution Office, which was actually engaged in the retail and wholesale of (morphine drugs). In addition to being the boss, Zhang Jinbiao also served as the general manager, appointed Han Bangjie as the engineer with a monthly salary of 100 yuan, and served as the business director of the wholesale office, responsible for the full authority of promoting morphine drugs. He also invited Zheng Shungen, a major shareholder residing at No. 15 Yihe Lane, Beile Road, in the French Concession, and the so-called engineer Han Bangjie to be responsible for purchasing the raw materials for manufacturing drugs. The daily output was shocking. In addition to hiring Zhang Kebei from Nantong as the clerk of the Hongkang Soap Factory Distribution Office (i.e., the drug wholesale facility), he also employed Sun Decheng, Wang Lifu from Ningbo, and Xue Desan from Changzhou as employees, and Ye Arui from Ningbo, who resided at Yongxiang Tobacco and Paper Store in Hujia Wood Bridge, as the cook. Liu Yongsong from Funing was the outgoing clerk. Zhang Lao Ban and the engineers had a car with the municipal government permit number "1952" and the concession permit number "10361" for their use. Zhang Jinbiao and others (shared the profits) made a lot of money and were very extravagant. Leader Chen and others used an axe to break open the back door and rushed in, bravely arresting the morphine drug criminals Zhang Jinbiao, Han Bangjie, Zhang Kebei, Sun Facheng, Wang Lifu, Liu Yongsong, Shen Xiaoliang, Xue Deshan, Ye Arui, and others. They confiscated (finished morphine) in four large packages weighing approximately 200 taels, another 200 taels of morphine that had not yet been produced in jars, as well as all the machinery, production equipment, and sundries. Several police officers were assigned to be temporarily guarded, and personnel were sent to take photos for the record. They also seized a car at the wholesale office at No. 26 Linping Road and took it to the team. At 9:00 AM yesterday, Captain Lu summoned all nine defendants to the case for preliminary interrogation. Japanese Residents Prefer Chinese Barber Shops

Because of Their Lower Prices

According to the Japanese-language "Mainichi Shimbun," there are 17 or 18 barber shops operated by Japanese merchants in the English and French Concessions that cater mainly to foreigners, and 15 that cater mainly to Japanese residents in Hongkou. However, there are also many Chinese barber shops that cater to Japanese residents. The prices of Chinese barber shops are less than half of those of Japanese merchants. Therefore, Japanese residents all go to Chinese-operated shops, and almost no one patronizes those operated by Japanese merchants. In addition, Japanese merchants have no strategy for attracting customers and developing their businesses, which has led to a sharp decline in business, it is said.

After Her Husband Returned to China, He Still Ignored Her, and the Woman Had No Choice But to Sue Him in Court 150

Huang Baoqiong, a 31-year-old woman from Guangdong, residing at No. 47 Hengshun Lane, Xigaota Road, is a graduate of Shanghai Nanyang Women's Commercial Middle School and has a considerable foundation in both Chinese and English. On March 15th of the Republic Era tenth year [1921], she married Ye Hongnian (currently 33 years old) from the same hometown through a matchmaker. Ye was a student studying in the United States. Before a year had passed, Ye went to the United States to do business, and at this time, Huang was already several months pregnant. Soon she gave birth to a son, named Genyin. However, her mother-in-law and sister-in-law often abused her. In addition to barely providing food and drink, her clothes were separate and ignored, and were borne by Huang's mother. Unexpectedly, Ye Hongnian did not return home after ten years abroad and consistently ignored her support. In the spring of the Republic Era twenty-first year [1932], she raised travel expenses and went to the United States alone to find him. After many twists and turns, she was finally found, but Ye was very cunning and had no feelings for her, treating her like a stranger. She had no choice but to sue in the American court, requesting a ruling to maintain her life. Unexpectedly, Ye also filed a counterclaim, requesting a ruling to divorce. The court ruled to suspend the litigation for one year. Huang had no money to stay, so she returned to Shanghai. Her mother-in-law and sister-in-law refused to take her in, so she had to live in her mother's house. Now that she heard that Ye had returned to China, she hired lawyer Wu Zhenming to sue Ye in the First Special Court, requesting a divorce and demanding payment of 25,400 yuan for clothing and other expenses for the past thirteen years and for Genyin's upbringing, 34,800 yuan for alimony (100 yuan per month, calculated for 29 years), and 7,600 yuan for Genyin's future education expenses, totaling 65,800 yuan. Yesterday, Judge Peng Shi held a hearing, but Ye still did not arrive. The court ordered another public notice to be served before a judgment was made.

Strict Prohibition of Trafficking in Opium and Drugs on Two Railway Lines 152

The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration issued instructions to the Vehicle Affairs Department, the Machinery Department, and the Police Department, stating that it had received Instruction No. 11238 from the Ministry of Railways, stating that according to the Railway Police Administration's report, Yang Baotang, a stoker from the Machinery Department of the railway, was found to be trafficking in opium. It was ordered that the stoker be immediately dismissed as a warning to others. From now on, all railway employees are strictly prohibited from trafficking in opium and drugs, whether taxed or untaxed. If anyone violates this order, whether on the station, on the train, en route, or in their residence, or in any other place, they shall be immediately dismissed and sent to the court or the official anti-narcotics agency for legal action, depending on the severity of the circumstances, in order to rectify discipline. This is to be strictly enforced without any regard or hesitation. In addition to reporting that Yang Baotang has been dismissed by the Machinery Department, this order is hereby given to the relevant departments to comply with it. In the future, such incidents must be strictly investigated and prohibited in order to rectify discipline and maintain the reputation of the railway. This order is hereby given.

Homicide Caused by Property Dispute Concluded

Police Lawyer Stated Newly Discovered Doubts, Defendant Wu Xihou Released on Bail of 1,000 Yuan 157

Wu Xihou, a local residing at No. 36 Maqi Road, Huxi, opposed his uncle Wu Gengsheng and cousins dividing the ancestral property located near his home in order to sell it, hoping to preserve the only ancestral property. However, Gengsheng and others did not understand, and on the 19th of last month, they invited land guarantor Wang Maomao and requested the Land Bureau to send five surveyors to survey the land. Xihou still intended to stop them and was beaten by Gengsheng and others, suffering injuries to his head and fingers. Xihou, seeing that he was outnumbered, fled home. Gengsheng then led his sons and nephews, Wu Fusheng and others, and nieces and nephews, nine men and women, into Xihou's home to cause trouble, destroying the furniture in the living room. Xihou then took out his self-defense pistol and fired a shot into the air. The gun was snatched away by Fusheng. At this time, the Chinese police officer on duty at Post No. 1924 near Wu's house arrived after hearing the alarm and was about to collect the seized pistol from Fusheng. Wu Wangshi, Wu Xihou's wife, who was standing opposite Fusheng, was suddenly shot and (fell to the ground dead). Afterwards, the police accused Wu Xihou of attempting to kill his uncle Wu Gengsheng and accidentally killing his wife and prosecuted him in the First Special District Local Court. The case has been reported repeatedly. However, Judge Zhan Liangce, who presided over the trial, attached great importance to it. The interrogation was very detailed, and he felt it was necessary to conduct an on-site inspection of the crime scene. Therefore, last Friday, he summoned the relevant witnesses and the Chinese and Western detectives in charge of the case, and invited the police prosecutor Zhang Tianyin and the defendant's defense lawyers Zhou Xiao'an and Fan Gang to Wu Xihou's house to conduct a detailed inspection. He ordered Wu Gengsheng and Wu Fusheng to demonstrate their positions at the time and also ordered the Chinese police officer No. 1924 to report the distance between Wu Fusheng and the deceased Wu Wangshi at the time he witnessed them facing each other and the position of Fusheng holding the seized (pistol). He then drove back to the court. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhan continued to hold a hearing and first summoned land guarantor Wang Maomao. According to his testimony, the five surveyors from the Land Bureau had been notified, but none of them were present in court today. At that time, he and the five were standing at the entrance of Wu Alin's house and only heard the gunshot and did not see the person who fired the shot. Then he summoned the Chinese police officer No. 1924. According to his testimony, he was on duty at the time, and a man in his thirties wearing a blue cloth shirt and pants reported to him. He rushed to Wu's house, and a Western police officer had arrived before him. At that time, the defendant waved to him and said that he was not a robber. Because the reporter said there were three pistols, he ordered the Western police officer to monitor the defendant, while he proceeded to investigate. At the east entrance, he saw Wu Fusheng standing facing north, and Wu Wangshi standing facing south. Fusheng was holding the pistol with the muzzle pointing at Wu Wangshi. He then ordered Fusheng to give him the gun. Unexpectedly, in an instant, when he looked back, Wu Wangshi had been shot and fell to the ground. However, this type of pistol does not make a sound when it hits the body. Wang Maomao and others said they heard (two gunshots), which is definitely not accurate. The court can test it to prove it, he said. When asked, Wu Gengsheng testified that the defendant fired three shots, all aimed at him. Wu Fusheng testified that the pistol was seized from the defendant's hand in the living room. Because there was no one in the living room, he ran out with the gun and did not see Wu Wangshi or know where she came from, and did not hear her cry in pain. The defendant Wu Xihou testified that he had never used the gun before, and this was the first time he had used it. He only fired one shot into the air. At that time, there were nine men and women on the other side, who chased into his house, and he had already been injured, so he had to take out the gun for self-defense. If the land guarantor had stopped them from chasing at this time, they might have listened, but he did not stop them, which led to his wife being killed. The court then ordered the debate to begin. The police lawyer Zhang Tianyin spoke first, saying that there were many doubts in this case. As far as the part of the complaint that the defendant attempted to kill Wu Gengsheng but failed, when conducting the on-site inspection, Gengsheng's demonstration of the situation was inconsistent with his previous testimony in court.

Recently, the Wu Zhou Pharmacy, in light of the economic decline in our country and the hardship of the people's lives, and considering that tuberculosis is widespread, especially among primary school students in this city, where the number of patients reaches six or seven out of ten, has not only donated funds to the Municipal Education Bureau to assist with tuberculosis treatment in schools but has also specially offered a half-price discount on its meticulously crafted various tuberculosis treatment products. Details have already been published in this newspaper. It is understood that the local primary school authorities greatly admire the Wu Zhou Pharmacy's spirit of caring for students and concerning itself with the health of the nation. Furthermore, as the company's various tuberculosis products have long been recognized for their effectiveness, they have followed the instructions of the Municipal Education Bureau and are actively encouraging children to purchase and use them. It is said that this preferential treatment from the pharmacy will last for one year.

Continued Hearing of the Great Wall Record Company's Lawsuit Against Wang Rui Rong for Obstructing Commerce and Industry 160

Wang Rui Rong, a Ningbo native and manager of the Jinghua Optical Company at 163 Nanjing Road, was recently sued in the First Special Court by Zheng Zi Bao, manager of the Great Wall Record Company at 152 Henan Road, through lawyers Chen Qun and Yan Shi Hua, for obstructing commerce and industry, along with a private prosecution requesting Wang Rui Rong to pay damages of 72,496 yuan. The case had been examined once by Judge Zhan Liang Ce, who instructed both parties to mediate outside of court. While rescheduling was underway, the defendant attempted to reconcile with the plaintiff through intermediaries. However, because the defendant had not shown sufficient sincerity, Judge Huang Ri Sheng of the Fifth Criminal Court summoned both parties, each accompanied by their lawyers, to court for questioning at 10:25 AM. After Judge Huang took his seat, he immediately ordered the plaintiff to state the reasons for the prosecution. According to the plaintiff, Zheng Zi Bao, the Great Wall Record Company is a limited liability company with Zhang Xiao Lin as chairman and general manager, and Du Yue Sheng, Zhang Dan Ru, and others as directors, with himself as manager and Lu Han Bang as deputy manager. The company had registered with the Ministry of Industry and Commerce and the Trademark Bureau. The plaintiff previously entered into a contract with the German Jingming Factory, entrusting all recording and production technical work to them. Since its release, sales have been very brisk. The defendant, taking advantage of the opportunity of the occupation of the three northeastern provinces by foreign forces, colluded with the Jingming Factory through his Rui Sheng Company in Harbin to secretly change our Great Wall Records to the "Ronghua" brand with the "Imperial Crown" trademark, selling them in the three northeastern provinces. In January of this year, upon discovering the defendant's sabotage of the Great Wall Company's business, he contacted the defendant. The defendant, unable to conceal his actions, expressed his apologies and immediately telegraphed his apprentice, Wei Fu Bao (who was stationed in Harbin by the defendant), to stop the sale of counterfeit Ronghua records. As a result, the defendant took responsibility and promised not to issue them. The plaintiff reported the outcome of the negotiations to Chairman Zhang and the directors, who also did not want to pursue the matter further. Unexpectedly, in July of this year, it was discovered that the defendant was actually selling Ronghua records as Great Wall records in Harbin. We immediately sent personnel to purchase various counterfeit records, such as "Fenhe Bay," a duet by Cheng Yan Qiu and Wang Shao Lou, which have been brought to court today for review. Furthermore, the counterfeit record labels of the defendant stated the words "Shanghai Ronghua Company," but there is no office in this city. Everything is under the control of the defendant alone. Therefore, the defendant cannot claim that the company is in Harbin and not under the jurisdiction of this court. The reason the previous court instructed mediation was because the defendant claimed that the place of sale of the counterfeit records was in Harbin, and the Shanghai court had no jurisdiction. His intention was to use the power of the Japanese puppets to undermine Chinese law. Therefore, our company's Chairman Zhang opposed mediation and firmly insisted that this court punish the defendant as he deserves. Following this, the defendant Wang Rui Rong stated that the Harbin Rui Sheng Company is managed by his student, Wei Fu Bao, and that he is only one of the shareholders. There is no office in Shanghai. In January of this year, when the plaintiff Zheng Zi Bao and Lu Han Bang spoke to me about counterfeiting, I immediately, out of friendship, telegraphed Wei Fu Bao to stop the sale of Ronghua records. As for the rest, I plead ignorance. The plaintiff then stated that the defendant's telegram to his apprentice Wei Fu Bao contained the words "The Ronghua records have arrived, not a single one needs to be released, and not a single one must be sold. If you disobey, I will come to Harbin myself." He asked the court to pay attention to the meaning of the four words "come to Harbin myself." After examining the words, Judge Huang instructed that the case still needed to be investigated and rescheduled the hearing for the 13th of this month.

Robbery with Firearms on Xin Zha Road, Housewife Wounded in the Face 161

At 10:20 last night, four robbers speaking mixed dialects suddenly entered the Fu Jian Gui Yuan Store at 289 Xin Zha Road (across from the Niao Zhen Road Bridge). Three of the robbers were armed with handguns and ordered everyone to remain silent. It is estimated that over 30 yuan in cash (in small change) was stolen, and the robbers fled through the door with their loot. Before the robbers had gone far, the housewife of the store shouted for the police. One of the robbers, hearing the shout, turned back and fired a shot at the woman, the bullet grazing her left cheekbone. Her skin was broken and bleeding, but fortunately, the injury was not internal. The robbers seized the opportunity to escape without a trace. Afterwards, the shop owner reported the incident to the police and requested a pursuit. The wounded woman was sent to Guangren Hospital for treatment.

Shanghai-Minhang Bus Overturns into a River 162

Yesterday afternoon at around 2:00 PM, a China Great Automobile Company driver, Zhang Yong Nian, was driving bus number 4607, carrying two passengers surnamed Li, from Shanghai to Minhang. When the bus reached the Mao Jia Wan area west of the Qian Liang Miao stop on the Shanghai-Minhang South Zhejiang Road, the driver was careless, causing the bus to overturn into the river beside the road, with the wheels facing upwards. Shanghai Telephone Bureau Selects Trainee Technicians 163

The Shanghai Telephone Bureau, recognizing that all telephone technicians are divided into cable workers and machine workers, with cable workers unfamiliar with machinery and machine workers unable to climb poles to repair telephone lines, each having their shortcomings, and that most have more experience than telephone knowledge, recruited trainee technicians in September of last year. The following nine people were admitted: Wang Rong Jin, Lu Bao Gan, Yao Shao An, Hua Shan, Qian Xiang, Li Chun Ren, Xu Ren Ze, Song Zi Ming, Cai Zi Run. Engineers from the bureau served as instructors, and after a year of training, the trainees recently took an examination. The examination was divided into oral and written tests. The oral test was personally administered by Director Xu Xue Yu, and all technicians were able to answer fluently, understanding telephone machinery, internal and external line conditions, and principles. The written test was administered by the engineers. Once the papers have been graded, they will be submitted to the ministry for formal employment. It is reported that the trainees performed well on the examination, and Director Xu commended them. Currently, there is a shortage of such talent in the country, and it is in great demand. It is planned to continue recruiting and training trainees in the near future in order to cultivate them.

Red Pill Manufacturing and Trafficking Case Cracked on Avenue Edward VII, Trial Concluded 164

Feng Zhi Ming, a Chinese detective from the anti-narcotics department of the General Patrol Office, along with detectives Wu Han Zhang and Bai Pu, cracked a major red pill manufacturing and trafficking operation on Avenue Edward VII at number 1400 and 62 Zilaihuo Street, Lane 6 in the French Concession, arresting seven suspects: Shen Bao Qian, Zhang Rong Sheng, Luo Zeng Sheng, Chen A Er, Xu Er Da, Xia He Sheng, and Lu Zhong Wen. Sixty pounds of red pills, a can of red dye, a pound of rock candy, a complete set of manufacturing equipment, and eight drying trays were confiscated and taken to the Chengdu Road Police Station for detention. Yesterday morning, the suspects were escorted to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court, and police lawyer Zhang Tian Yin not only prosecuted the defendants under Article 6 of the Anti-Smoking Law but also described the circumstances of the case in detail, stating that at 6:15 AM yesterday, police detectives first arrested the defendant Shen Shen Qian at the intersection of Avenue Edward VII and Ma Huo Road and found five bags of red pills, totaling three pounds, hidden in the white belt around his waist. According to Shen's confession, the red pills were given to him by Zhang Rong Sheng, the director of the factory at 1400 Avenue Edward VII. The detectives then requested a search warrant from the court and secretly conducted a search, arresting Zhang, Luo, Chen, and Xu. Zhang pointed out that all the red pills and machines were hidden in a secret door. The secret door was located above the floor, so the police used a bamboo ladder to climb to the floor and open the secret door. Inside, there was indeed a manufacturing workshop, large in scale. A large number of machines and red pills were confiscated. Shen Bao Qian stated that the factory was opened by someone named "Little Baozi," and Zhang Rong Sheng was the director, responsible for everything in the factory. He was also hired by Zhang, delivering five bags of red pills to Lu Zhong Wen at 62 Zilaihuo Street, Lane 6, each day for a salary of twelve yuan per month. Luo Zeng Sheng was a pharmacist, and Chen and Xu were workers. Zhang also implicated Xia He Sheng. The police then arrested Zhang. Xia denied any involvement in the red pill manufacturing at the police station, claiming that "Little Baozi" (originally named Wang De Rong) had borrowed 500 yuan from him, but had not repaid it, leading to his implication. However, the police did find Wang's IOU in Xia's home. Later, Lu Zhong Wen was arrested at 62 Zilaihuo Street. However, Little Baozi escaped. The seized items were then presented for inspection. Shen Bao Qian confessed that he was hired by Little Baozi to deliver red pills, a total of three times, five bags each time. Zhang Rong Sheng confessed to manufacturing red pills for a monthly salary of ten yuan. Luo Zeng Sheng confessed to helping with the manufacturing for a monthly salary of fifteen yuan. Chen A Er stated that he was a tea server for a monthly salary of ten yuan. Xu Er Da stated that he was a cook and did not know about the red pill manufacturing. Xia He Sheng claimed that he was being framed because Little Baozi had borrowed 500 yuan from him to return to his hometown to marry a wife, but had not repaid it to this day, so he was framed. Lu Zhong Wen's confession was vague. After Judge Zhan Liang Ce examined the confessions, he announced the end of the hearing and scheduled sentencing for next Wednesday. Xia was released on bail of 500 yuan, and the rest were remanded.

Accused of Abusing Wife

Private Torture, Beating, and Chaining of Feet, Mother Claims Daughter-in-Law Has a Lover 166

At 4:45 PM yesterday, the Zhongxing Road Police Station of the Xin Zha Public Security Bureau received a report that Xu Yu Cai, a weaver residing at 1238 Zhongxing Road, was privately torturing his wife, withholding food and drink, and chaining her feet. Police officers Wang Ying Wen and others were dispatched to the scene and found Xu's wife chained up in the bedroom. However, Xu Yu Cai had already fled, feeling guilty. Xu's mother, Feng, and Xu's wife, Zhu Er Mei (i.e., Xu Zhu), were taken to the station for questioning and then transferred to the Xin Zha Bureau. Officer Zheng Zu Han questioned Xu Zhu, who stated that she was 18 years old, earned her living by weaving, and that Xu Yu Cai accused her of having a lover and often beat her. For the past few days, he had chained both her feet inside the room and withheld food and drink. Fortunately, someone reported it to the police station, and she was rescued. She requested that Xu Yu Cai be arrested and prosecuted and that Xu planned to sell her to someone surnamed for 250 yuan. Xu Feng stated that she was 53 years old and Feng Zhu was her daughter-in-law. Because she was having an affair with a rice shop worker, her son had chained her up in the room, and there was no intention to sell her. Now her son's whereabouts are unknown. After examining the confessions, the interrogating officer stated that there was no proof of whether she had a lover. However, Xu Yu Cai's act of chaining Zhu's feet was an abuse of private torture and was inappropriate. In addition to releasing Xu Zhu's feet and summoning Xu Yu Cai to answer the charges, Xu Zhu, Xu Feng, and the chains were sent to the Public Security Bureau for disposition.

Success of Public Address System, Practical Application of Chinese Bookkeeping 167

The Chinese Bookkeeping Improvement Course, jointly organized by the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and accountant Xu Yong Zuo, has been running since August 1st and concluded the day before yesterday after two months. Students sent from other cities have also packed their bags and returned home. The course had over 760 students, and the classroom was the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Auditorium. It was not easy to have the entire class listening in the same classroom. A public address system was specially designed and installed by the China Wireless Research Society to transmit the sound. Therefore, the lecturer could speak in a normal tone, and the students, regardless of the distance of their seats, could hear clearly. The students in this course achieved excellent results, which may be attributed to the equipment of the public address system. Principal and chief lecturer Xu Yong Zuo praised this machine as a powerful tool for lectures and planned to introduce it widely to promote the progress of science in our country.

Two Announcements from the Hydrographic Bureau 169

The Hydrographic Bureau issued two navigation announcements yesterday, stating: (1) In the Zhenjiang to Nanjing section of the Yangtze River, the Huanglian Port buoy has been moved due to the collapse of the riverbank at that location. Its new position is at a distance of 1.39 nautical miles at 12 degrees north of the Niaolong Temple, i.e., approximately 118 degrees 53 minutes east longitude and 32 degrees 11 minutes north latitude. (2) On the east coast, at the west entrance of the Sanpandong Mentou Gorge, its position is at a distance of 2 chains (every 10 chains equals 1 nautical mile) at 26 degrees north of the Niushi Reef, i.e., approximately 121 degrees 5 minutes east longitude and 27 degrees 49 minutes north latitude. There used to be a shipwreck obstructing ships, but it has now been salvaged.

Letter 178

Dear Sir, Our Old Overseas Chinese Relief Association is currently planning to send a representative, Mr. Atlassov, to solicit donations in various places in the Far East outside of Shanghai in the near future, and to solicit various advertisements for a book published by our association, "Travel Records of Various Places in the Far East." All the donations solicited and the various advertising fees collected in the book of travel records will be used by our association, according to the agreement, only for old overseas Chinese, poor and helpless young students, and soldiers injured and disabled during the European War. We believe that your country and the Chinese men and women and the Chinese government agencies and commercial companies in various places in the Far East will surely express deep sympathy for these old overseas Chinese aged 70 to 80 or older, as well as poor students and disabled soldiers, and will be happy to contribute, so that small contributions can be gathered together, so that these helpless people can survive. Our association, on behalf of the old overseas Chinese, young students, and disabled soldiers, respectfully expresses our sincere gratitude to the Chinese men and women, and we are also deeply grateful to your newspaper for not hesitating to publish our announcement. We hereby express our thanks. This is addressed to the editor of the Shen Bao. Respectfully submitted by Papaf, Chairman of the Old Overseas Chinese Relief Association, and Valsamov, Secretary.

Reading Q&A

From Essays to the Sun Yat-sen Culture and Education Center Quarterly (Continued) 179

As for the Sun Yat-sen Culture and Education Center Quarterly, in this publishing world flooded with essays, it is natural to acknowledge that it has considerable value, although there are a few articles inside that we do not necessarily need. The articles pointed out by Mr. Lin are also the most worthwhile to read in the journal. Therefore, it cannot be said that it is not beneficial to readers to examine the content of these articles.

First, let's talk about Mr. Li Shicen's article "The Trend of World Thought." This article discusses in detail the various schools of thought in the world's current six major cultural fields, such as philosophy, science, and art. Needless to say, we can get a general overview of the world's cultural trends here. This kind of comprehensive introduction is very necessary for us, because our general research ability is limited, and it is of great help to us to see the general trend of the world in a relatively short article. However, if the scope is too large, it is difficult to say that it is complete. Mr. Li's article naturally has many shortcomings. On the whole, although he told us at the beginning that the source of the entire trend of world thought is the rise of the oppressed and suffering masses, that is to say, the movement of world thought is based on social relations. But in the whole article, when he analyzed the various schools, he did not fully explain the occurrence of each school with social reasons, but only listed them one by one in theory. When he criticized the incorrect schools, he only argued from the theoretical standpoint and could not fully expose their social nature. In fact, all theories are rooted in society, and only by clearly analyzing its significance and role in society can its essence be truly explained. Relying solely on theoretical debate cannot complete the task of criticism. In the parts about religion and education, this shortcoming is relatively small, but in the parts about philosophy and science, Mr. Li Shicen's article cannot fulfill this task. This point must be pointed out. Because the relationship between religion, education, etc., and society is relatively obvious, everyone knows that social reasons must be used to explain them. Philosophy and science are more inclined to theory, although this theory will eventually have a social effect. The general old scientists and philosophers always deceive us by saying that science and philosophy are things that transcend society and are purely academic subjects that have nothing to do with social relations. In order to oppose this kind of deception, our analysis of the social nature of science and philosophy should be more important than religion, education, etc. Although we cannot ignore this aspect of religion, education, etc., for the reasons mentioned above, we cannot but put more effort into the aspects of science and philosophy. Mr. Li Shicen's article did not achieve this step, which is a big shortcoming.

Secondly, this article narrates world thought only from the horizontal aspect, listing the various schools of thought, and does not narrate the development status of each school from the vertical aspect. Although he pointed out that the trend of world thought is towards the direction of dialectics, he did not say anything about the path taken by these thoughts towards this direction. Therefore, it is better to say that this is narrating the various "schools" of world thought than to say that this is talking about the "trend" of world thought. It cannot completely fit the original meaning of the topic, especially since it is quite contradictory to the fundamental standpoint (dialectics) taken by Mr. Li Shicen when writing this article. Dialectical philosophy itself is developed and strengthened in movement and struggle. It is not a dead truth that has been cast. But in Mr. Li Shicen's article, this state of development cannot be seen. There, dialectical philosophy seems to be several kinds of mutually independent theories with other schools, but only it is more correct. As for what is the difference between the dialectical philosophy of the 19th century and the dialectical philosophy of the 20th century, and what progress the latter has made, it is also impossible to know. It is very incompatible with the original meaning of "trend."

Educational News

Forthcoming Chinese Art Exhibition in London 189

▲ Initiated Following the Example of France, Italy, Belgium, and the Netherlands

▲ Scheduled to Be Held in England for Sixteen Weeks Beginning November of Next Year

▲ Executive Yuan Resolves to Establish a Preparatory Committee to Organize Everything

In recent years, London has held several international art exhibitions, including those of Italy, France, Belgium, Persia, the Netherlands, and Finland.

The purpose of these exhibitions is to reflect the spirit of various nations' lives over the years, and to demonstrate the achievements of their creative abilities, so that visitors can understand the relative positions of each nation, thereby promoting international friendship and leading to substantial benefits in politics, economics, and even commerce. Their value is well-established. China's art and culture has a long history, and its achievements are the most abundant and outstanding. Its essence as a representative of Eastern spiritual civilization is enough to stimulate Western thought that is highly focused on material development. Therefore, the China Committee of British Universities and members of the British academic community, this spring

Suggested to the Chinese Minister to England, Guo, to follow the example of other countries and hold a large-scale international Chinese art exhibition in London to promote Chinese culture and enhance Sino-British relations. This suggestion was subsequently endorsed in principle by the governments of China and Britain. The British initiators then submitted several further proposals, offering plans. The Executive Yuan immediately designated the Ministry of Education to review the matter in conjunction with the Ministries of Foreign Affairs and Interior. After consultations between the Ministry of Education and Minister Guo, and after a joint meeting of the three ministries, it was agreed that this matter was of great importance and that China should first establish a preparatory committee for the London International Exhibition of Chinese Art, directly under the Executive Yuan, to be responsible for the organization. Seven preparatory measures were drafted and submitted to the 177th meeting of the Executive Yuan for approval, and reported to the Central Political Council for record. Now, upon investigation, regarding the

Exhibition Organization, it is formally jointly supervised by the central governments of the two countries, with the Royal Academy of Arts managing the exhibition affairs. The heads of state of the two countries will be supervisors, and the heads of the executive branches of the two countries, political and social leaders of both countries, and ministers of foreign affairs, interior, finance, and education will be honorary presidents or deputy supervisors. A board of directors will be established to manage all matters. Regarding the chairman of the board of directors, Sir Lee Tun has recently been nominated. The vice-chairmen and directors will be appointed equally by China and Britain. Under the board of directors, there will be a secretariat and selection, transportation, arrangement, publicity, and finance groups to handle various matters separately.

Preparatory Committee Organization established separately by China is set to include the secretary-general or chief of the political affairs department of the Executive Yuan, the vice ministers of interior, foreign affairs, finance, and education, and the director of the Palace Museum as ex officio members. A chairman will be appointed by the Executive Yuan to preside over the affairs of the committee, with the vice ministers of interior, foreign affairs, and education as standing committee members. Underneath will be a secretary-general and one Chinese and one English secretary. In addition, there will be seven to eleven expert committee members, to be selected by the chairman from domestic art experts in the future. There will be several staff members, divided into groups to handle affairs. It will be established shortly.

Exhibition Period has been provisionally set to begin in November of next year and end in March of the 25th year of the Republic of China, for a total of sixteen weeks, which is six weeks longer than any previous international art exhibition. The location is set at the Royal Academy of Arts' Burlington House in London, where previous exhibitions have been held. The building is magnificent in structure and well-suited for the purpose.

Exhibited Items will, as in previous cases, mainly consist of treasures from the museums run by the national and provincial governments of the respective countries, and supplemented by collections from international organizations and private individuals. This exhibition will focus on the collections of the Palace Museum and the Antiquities Preservation Institute, and will also solicit selections from museums and collectors around the world. The items to be sent for exhibition by China will be selected by Chinese and British experts according to a set procedure, and the packing will be supervised and guided by experts. They will be transported to England in batches. The loading and unloading of ships, and the transportation from the docks to the exhibition venue, will be carefully arranged with strict security measures. Storage in England will be at the Royal Academy of Arts vault, which has iron doors and is guarded day and night by a sufficient security team, ensuring utmost safety. Regarding the

Exhibition Expenses, according to the British experience of the past six times, the expenses for preparation, transportation, insurance, and exhibition can be covered by the future ticket sales revenue. Before the opening, the Royal Academy of Arts will temporarily advance the funds, so there is no need to allocate additional funds.

Exhibition Results, if there is a surplus, a portion will be paid to the Royal Academy of Arts, and the remainder will be jointly decided by the Chinese side and the British initiators for use in Sino-British cultural projects. Previous exhibitions lasted only ten weeks, but attracted more than 1.5 million visitors and achieved good results. This is the first time that the spirit of Chinese art and culture will be presented on a large scale internationally in Europe. If fully supported and properly organized by both the public and private sectors in China, it will surely attract even greater attention from Europeans.

It is also reported that the preparatory committee will soon hold a preparatory meeting in Beijing to discuss and begin all preparatory matters.

Provinces and major cities should focus on the implementation of labor education

▲ Instructions from the Ministries of Industry and Education 190

The Ministries of Industry and Education jointly issued a circular on the 2nd to the education and construction departments of various provinces, as well as the construction, education, and social bureaus of various cities, stating: "According to the proposal submitted by the Labor Education Design Committee regarding the implementation of labor education by social education institutions in cities, and the establishment of labor education centers in major cities to improve the lives of workers and promote labor education, please review and implement. Upon reviewing the original proposal, it is for the purpose of promoting labor education. Regarding the establishment of labor education centers in major cities as mentioned in the original measures, the education administrative agencies of various provinces and cities should handle it according to their financial capacity. Regarding the objects of education in cities, attention should be paid to workers and various factories. The labor education implementation institutions should be assisted as much as possible and should not be deliberately obstructed. The administrative agencies of various provinces and cities should supervise their subordinates to implement these measures conscientiously. In addition to separate orders, the original proposal is copied and issued for compliance."

▲ Attached is the full text of the proposal: Social education implementation institutions in cities should focus on the implementation of labor education, and labor education centers should be established in major cities to improve the lives of workers and promote labor education. The reasons are: (1) The number of social education implementation institutions in China has been increasing in recent years. The education objects of social education institutions in cities often focus on a small number of citizens, while ignoring the laboring masses who most need to improve their lives and lack knowledge. This approach makes the educational content of urban social education institutions feel empty and impractical, and at the same time, the laborers need education but cannot obtain it, which is a major flaw. Therefore, urban social education institutions should strive to correct this shortcoming and focus on the implementation of labor education. In major cities, labor education implementation institutions should be specially established to handle the implementation of labor education, so that labor education can be popularized as soon as possible and the lives of workers can be improved. (2) Measures: (A) It is recommended that the Ministry of Education issue a circular to the education administrative agencies of various provinces and cities, stating that urban social education institutions should focus on laborers as their education objects, and must go deep into the labor force to handle labor education. In major cities, labor education centers should be specially established to handle the implementation of labor education. (B) It is recommended that the Ministry of Industry issue a circular to various factories, stating that they should assist labor education implementation institutions as much as possible, encourage laborers to receive education, and should not deliberately obstruct their work. (Resolution passed)
