Personal Views on Implementing Productive Education (2) Stenographic Record by Wang Gongxia 195

▲ Speech by Director Pan Gongzhan of the Education Bureau at the General Meeting of the Third District Education Association of this City

If we believe this path is correct, how should we implement it? Of course, we cannot rely on one or two individuals or a small group of people to implement it. We must rely on a group of educators, working together with one heart and one mind, to achieve the goal. However, can this productive education be implemented leisurely? Can we wait until we have raised a large amount of funds before implementing it? I can say that it is absolutely impossible. If we implement it leisurely, this year will be too late, and we will prepare again next year. If next year is too late, we will prepare again the year after that. In this way, two, three... eight or nine years will pass. By that time, even if we want to implement it, we will not have the opportunity. Because we are muddling through, while foreign countries are making rapid progress. Foreigners drive cars, while we ride wheelbarrows. How can we catch up? Therefore, time does not allow us to implement productive education leisurely. Some people say that since time requires us to implement it quickly, we should first ask the government to provide a large amount of funds to ensure the independence of education funds and increase the proportion of allocation, not only this year but also increasing year by year, so that we can implement productive education quickly. This is also impossible, because China is a poor country, a bankrupt country. Everything has almost been pawned and sold out. We do not even have enough food to eat. To take out a large amount of money to implement productive education would be like a dream. Not to mention a large amount of funds, it would be a great fortune if the existing funds could be paid without being in arrears. Jiangsu and Zhejiang are among the most prosperous provinces in the country, but this year, both Jiangsu and Zhejiang have suffered droughts. The land tax will be discounted, and the land tax surcharge will also be lost. Many elementary schools in inland towns and villages cannot even open their doors. How can they take out a large amount of funds to implement productive education? Some people say that if the government cannot provide money, we can ask the people to provide money themselves. But where does the government's money come from? Because the people have no money, the government has no money. How can the people take out money to implement productive education? We understand this principle and can know that there must be two prerequisites for implementing productive education in China at present. One prerequisite is to be fast, to be agile, not to wait for next year if we can do it this year, and not to wait for the year after that if we can do it next year. Another prerequisite is that we cannot implement large-scale, magnificent, and luxurious productive education like wealthy countries such as Britain and the United States. China can only use the method of a bankrupt family, saving money to implement productive education. That is, we must be agile and economical. This is indeed a very difficult task. However, we must understand that if it were easy to do, if we had one million yuan and could open three or five productive schools or vocational schools in Shanghai, then two or three hundred thousand yuan would open one school. Anyone could do it. We would not be needed to do it. Now, it is precisely because we have no money, we must be fast, and we must do it well, so everyone should discuss and study a method, and then implement it step by step. Recently, Mr. Wu Zhihui published an article in the Morning Post, saying, "We must be able to catch up even if we have no money." This method, which he painstakingly instructed us, is the method that China truly needs at present.

The Prince of Makassar, Malaya, Comes to China Admiring Chinese Culture and Studies in Shanghai 198

▲ Visited the Director of the Municipal Education Bureau Yesterday to Explain His Intentions

▲ Director Pan Introduced Him to Study at Tongji University

Prince Anhui Sultan of the Makassar royal family in British Malaya has now arrived in Shanghai. His purpose in coming to Shanghai is to admire Chinese culture and to study in China to seek further education. After arriving in Shanghai, the prince stayed at Room 319 of the New Asia Hotel. He visited Director Pan Gongzhan of the Municipal Education Bureau in the city center yesterday morning. Director Pan personally received him and treated him with courtesy. The prince stated that he came to China on the recommendation of Wang Defen, our country's consul-general in the area, and wanted to enter a famous Chinese university. After hearing Pan's talk, he has been introduced to study at Tongji University in Wusong. It is reported that there are 1.2 million overseas Chinese in the Malay Peninsula. It is expected that when Prince Anhui completes his studies and returns to his country, it will further strengthen the relationship between the two nations.

A New Page in Shanghai's Municipal Construction

Wu Tiecheng's Speech 199

▲ The Significance of the Groundbreaking Ceremony for the Shanghai Municipal Stadium Gymnasium Swimming Pool ▲ Ladies and gentlemen, today is the groundbreaking ceremony for the Shanghai Municipal Stadium Gymnasium Swimming Pool held by the Shanghai Municipal Government. I am very honored and grateful for the presence of representatives from all walks of life to participate in the ceremony.

Shanghai has been under construction as a modern metropolis for more than ninety years. Seventy or eighty years ago, the population of the area around Shanghai County's Nanshi was only more than 40,000, and the concessions had only a few hundred people. After seventy or eighty years of development, the population of Shanghai has now reached more than 3.4 million, of which only about 70,000 or 80,000 are foreigners. Of these 3.4 million, those living in the municipal district account for more than three-fifths of the total, while those living in the public concessions account for only less than two-fifths. Of the total population of Shanghai, Chinese people account for more than 98%, while foreigners account for only less than 2%. Although Chinese people living in the concessions are bound by various regulations of the concessions, they are still protected by Chinese law. From this point of view, although Shanghai has concessions, the population of the concessions accounts for only less than two-fifths of the total population of the city, and more than 90% of them are Chinese. Therefore, the masters of Shanghai are of course we Chinese, and those who can represent Shanghai and build Shanghai are of course also we Chinese.

Although Shanghai has been under construction as a modern metropolis for more than ninety years, the people of Shanghai at that time absolutely did not expect Shanghai to develop so quickly and have today's prosperity. Therefore, all past construction plans were very small and simple, especially for public facilities, so that all existing facilities cannot meet the needs of today's general public. Moreover, most of Shanghai's past construction was in the concessions, which can only be said to be the construction of the concessions. Therefore, when large ocean liners of 20,000 or 30,000 tons enter the Huangpu River in Shanghai today, it not only takes a lot of time, but also the maneuvering of the ship's body is very difficult, and the loading and unloading of passengers is also very inconvenient. Shanghai is one of the largest commercial ports for import and export in China. The import and export of all goods in Shanghai suffers direct and indirect losses of time and money due to the simple and crude facilities such as ship docks. Moreover, foreigners who come to Shanghai for sightseeing often cannot see the true face of China, because everything they see in the concessions, including the architecture, the people's way of life, customs, and habits, are almost the same as in Europe and the United States. Even the Chinese people living in the concessions have gradually become Europeanized. Although Shanghai is the fifth largest city in the world, and Shanghai's development is faster than other cities, Shanghai's construction, especially public facilities, has not kept pace with Shanghai's progress. Therefore, although Shanghai has the name of a modern metropolis, all public facilities are lagging behind, especially the cultural facilities. Peiping has a library, Guangzhou has a library, Nanjing has a sports field, and Qingdao has a sports field. Shanghai, a metropolis with a population of more than 3.4 million, a center of national economy and culture, and often regards itself as the leader of the country, has completely ignored such public facilities and important cultural construction. The Shanghai Municipal Government, in view of this, has jointly planned with people from all walks of life to build the various public facilities needed by Shanghai, in order to open a new page in Shanghai's municipal construction in the future. There are 20,000 to 30,000 students in Shanghai, and the number of schools in Shanghai is no less than that in Peiping, but the sports facilities are the simplest and can simply be said to be non-existent. Shanghai only has a racecourse, not a sports field. The racecourse is only a place for the leisure sports and entertainment of a few special classes. The places for entertainment and sports for ordinary people, especially for the physical education of our Chinese youth, are completely ignored. Judging from the rapidly developing situation in Shanghai, Shanghai's construction in the future should catch up and not be allowed to continue to be simple. Therefore, the Shanghai Municipal Government deeply knows that Shanghai's construction in the future should not only meet the needs of the general public in Shanghai, but also plan for Shanghai a hundred years later. We must concentrate the strength of all the people of Shanghai to seek the construction of a greater Shanghai. The Shanghai Municipal Government also deeply knows that Shanghai's construction in the future is to be borne by us Chinese ourselves. In view of the urgent need for sports fields and other sports facilities for the general public, especially for young students to exercise their bodies, we are preparing and proceeding in conjunction with people from all walks of life, first deciding on a plan, then raising funds, and starting to build sports gymnasiums and swimming pools. These three sports fields, gymnasiums, and swimming pools are the most needed facilities for all the people of Shanghai. We hope that because of these three sports facilities, sports can be popularized and developed day by day. We hope that all citizens, especially the general youth, will make full use of these facilities to live up to our expectations.

We all know that the fundamental mass movement in China today is the national rejuvenation movement. The way to national rejuvenation is to enrich the country and strengthen the people. However, to enrich the country, we must first strengthen the people. The most important thing is to carry out the movement to strengthen the people first. The various physical exercises in the sports fields, gymnasiums, and swimming pools are all methods of strengthening the people. The Shanghai Municipal Government will never forget its important responsibility, so even when the funds are very tight, we are especially carrying out the construction of these sports facilities needed for sports, both to live up to the hopes of our citizens and to show the beginning of Shanghai's cultural construction in the future, in order to seek the revival of the nation. October 1, 23rd year of the Republic of China.

The Problem of Autumn Clothing, Food, and Supplies 200

— Dao Qin

"The leaves fall from the wutong tree, the autumn air is clear, the azure sky is like water, and the moonlight is bright." These two lines tell us that the early autumn season, Mengqiu, is approaching the Zhongyuan Festival... In other words, it is precisely the season for us to change our clothes and food. Upon careful thought, during this time when the whole world is turning to autumn, the exchange of clothing and food, the tailoring and purchasing by people, and the financial implications undoubtedly represent an astonishing statistic. Its impact on the effectiveness of using domestic goods is bound to have an even closer relationship.

Although "promoting domestic goods" is an "old chestnut" of a saying, I think that since we are born as Chinese people, when changing our clothes and food in the autumn season, we should take the use of domestic products as a prerequisite for purchasing all clothing and food. Buying one portion of domestic goods is equivalent to increasing the country's vitality by one portion... Speaking of clothing, in this "瑟瑟 (sè sè - rustling) autumn wind" weather, everyone has the regret of "when the autumn wind rises, I have no clothes on my body." Therefore, adding clothing is an urgent and immediate problem. I earnestly wish that patriotic people, when adding suits, would mostly use domestic woolen fabrics from Zhanghua, Minsheng, and other brands. I earnestly wish that wise housewives, when purchasing clothing, would mostly use stylish and artistic fabrics from domestic brands such as Sanyou and Hongxin. It is both economical and patriotic, so why not do it?

As for food, because our stomachs have been irrigated with light flavors such as melons and fruits juices during the summer, rich-flavored foods have become a timely need and desire. In other words, autumn is the period when our appetite increases. Moreover, as the Mid-Autumn Festival approaches, there is even more activity of buying food to give as gifts. I further hope that patriotic ladies, when purchasing "food for consumption," should step into domestic goods companies and local product companies to purchase various domestic foods. Do not buy food from Japan, and do not eat fruits from the West, because buying one more portion of foreign goods means consuming one more portion of the country's vitality. Patriotic ladies, please carefully consider my words!

My Views on Purchasing Autumn Supplies 205

— Ba Ling

The double wheels of time are moving forward on the track, not favoring anyone. Now, it is "another easy year and the autumn wind is here again!" In autumn, the climate is getting colder day by day, and everything we wear and use must naturally adapt to the climate and be reformed and purchased! Alas! How difficult is it to purchase clothing and other items? If we purchase them rashly without considering them, then it is inevitable that we will be deceived by inferior goods disguised as good ones, send our hard-earned money into the hands of our enemies, and still suffer ourselves in the future. What is the point of that? Secondly, if we purchase autumn supplies carelessly and casually, we may not be completely deceived by inferior goods, but at least we must consider the quality of the goods in order to achieve the effect of "purchasing excellent goods with reasonable money." Therefore, at this time, Mr. Yang An, the editor of the Shenbao National Goods Weekly, has published this special issue on autumn supplies to meet the needs of the season, to discuss the issue of autumn supplies, and to point out the method of purchasing supplies. This is not a meaningless thing. Now, the author will write down some of my shallow experiences below as a small contribution. I don't know if it will win the sympathy of the readers?

(1) Purchasing supplies must be taught by domestic factories. "Using domestic goods is everyone's natural duty." The reporter has already said these two sentences so many times that they are rotten. There is no need to waste space now. We must purchase autumn supplies from domestic factories, because as far as I know, the products of domestic factories have indeed achieved excellent results, such as Jinglun Factory's brocade shirts, Wuhe Factory's cotton shirts, Zhenfeng Factory's spring and autumn shirts, and Sanyou Society's towel quilts. These are all necessary supplies in autumn. Those who want to purchase them may wish to try them on to know that my words are not false.

(2) Purchasing supplies must take into account one's ability. The so-called ability here refers to economic ability. Why must purchasing supplies take into account one's economic ability? Because there are some people who often do not take into account their economic ability. For example, when purchasing spring and autumn shirts, if their ability is not sufficient, then buying two to change and replace is fine. But they insist on showing off their wealth and have to buy three or four. As a result, their economic ability gradually becomes stretched. There are not a few such people in society. The ancients said, "Rather be thrifty than extravagant," which means to teach people to be appropriate. I think that when purchasing autumn supplies, we should also take into account our economic ability and reach an appropriate level.

Other things such as cosmetics needed by women do not need to be bought from foreign countries. Home Industry Cooperatives have excellent products. Gentlemen who like to have a small drink in autumn, Guanshengyuan and Taikang are very exquisite domestic canteens. Is it necessary to specialize in eating foreign goods and sending money abroad?

Domestic Felt Hats and "Top-Tossing Kung Fu" 207

— Rong Yu

As soon as the autumn wind rises, the scorching sun has retreated, and people don't need to wear "Panama" and "cork" and "pith" hats when they go out. But it is not very elegant to be bareheaded, so the felt hat came into being and flew to people's heads.

Beautiful and noble people like to buy foreign felt hats to wear. At the very least, they cost about ten yuan a piece. Ten yuan or thirty yuan is nothing. Wearing this kind of hat may not be beautiful to the extreme, but sending the good money to foreigners is really heartless to the extreme. Moreover, there is a kind of wretched person who snatches hats on the streets of Shanghai. Their code name is "Top-Tossing Kung Fu," and they specialize in snatching this kind of noble felt hat. Their eyes are really sharp. At first glance, they know the value of this hat. Unless you are sitting in a motor car, they always have a way to snatch it in their hands, whether on a tram or a rickshaw. Once a hat is in hand, like a player passing a leather ball, they escape from A to B, from B to C, disappearing without a trace. As for ordinary felt hats, they don't care about them at all.

In addition to being rough and hard, domestic felt hats are no less inferior to foreign products in terms of color and style... and they are cheap, and a hat can be sold for two or three yuan. It is very beautiful to wear on the head, and friends of "Top-Tossing Kung Fu" will never patronize it. Why don't you all wear it?

Everyone knows that domestic felt hats are cheap and beautiful. As for avoiding the danger of "Top-Tossing Kung Fu," no one has mentioned it before, but I am the first to invent it!

Free Talk

About the Words of "Wu Yan Ji Lian" 209

— Jin Zutong

A few days ago, Mr. Chen Zizhan mentioned the book "Wu Yan Ji Lian" by Wang Guanguo in his article "Records of Proverbs," and suspected that there was no engraved version... However, I have a copy in my collection, which I bought at a book stall by Daming Lake during my travels last year. It was reprinted by his (Wang Guanguo)'s great-grandsons Yixun and Shenrong in the twelfth year of Tongzhi. As for the woodblocks, they were still from the Jiaqing period. According to Yixun's preface...

...It was engraved since the Gengchen year of Jiaqing, and it has been widely circulated for more than fifty years. During the Xianfeng Gengshen calamity, the old residence of Laotieshan Village was destroyed by war, and fortunately, half of the rear corridor of the ancestral hall remained, and the text manuscripts and other woodblocks were preserved, losing only ten woodblocks... Now my brothers are trying to subsidize the reprinting to complete it...

It can be seen that it was once popular because of its vulgarity, but it was not regarded as a kind of knowledge. However, in that time when solemn appearance and simple learning were very prevalent... It was already very commendable to dare to engrave this kind of book, not afraid of the elders scolding it as a "disaster of jujube and plum!"

Because the discovery of folklore is only a little over ten years old, although it can be said to be the legacy of "historians collecting customs," under the rule of emperors at that time, within the traditional thought that "books should not be read before the Qin and Han dynasties, and words must be referred to as the Three Dynasties"... Proverbs and folklore always felt too remote and vulgar to be regarded as a kind of knowledge. His preface said...

...This book refers to the legacy of poetry and history, and uses praise and criticism to convey punishment, which is thought-provoking. It starts with colloquialism, which is easier to approach than books that persuade people to do good. It is really enough to be a maxim for awakening the world...

The same book has completely different perspectives and opinions from the past and the present!

According to Zhu Moxian's "Mingzhai Xiaoshi," it was written by Wang Guanguo because he felt many things in his hometown. However, this book only bears his alias "Cizhuang Sushi Ji." There are also two people who are "Gengyuan Sun Shi Can" and "Yunfeng Lu Shi Jiao" who did not mention their names. Even his two great-grandsons (reprint publishers) only signed "Yixun" and "Shenrong" in the preface, as if it was very unglamorous to print this kind of shallow book, so they were unwilling to mention their real names. From our current point of view, it is really somewhat incomprehensible.

If it were not for "Mingzhai Xiaoshi" saying that it was written by Wang Guanguo, wouldn't a author who had contributed to folklore be buried?

For example, Mr. Wu Fengsun, the author of "Yifa Tong" quoted by Mr. Chen Zizhan, is said to be an old celebrity. People used to say that "once you become a celebrity, you are no longer worth seeing." Therefore, the book of rumors and customs "Yifa Tong" written by this kind of celebrity was of course not worth seeing in the eyes of people in the past!

Regarding this kind of thing, with the gradual development of folklore, it will continue to be discovered. Let's record it to wait for future verification?

Quietness 210

— Yingzi

Lonely days are a little hard to endure.

I remember there is such a witty saying in India... "Happiness and worries have the same aversion for lonely people." Because it is like this, that loneliness can also be said to be for a kind of piercing, unbearable sadness...

What a truly submerged dreamland!

When I look back on the past, it is so unbearable to look back... And I grew up in such a deep and boundless environment.

However, there are also times when I am alert to my own soul.

At that time, our family lived in a deep alley. Every day, every day, in the clear dawn with a glimmer of light, whether in the wind or rain, there was always a voice reciting the Buddha's name, dragging a long, drawn-out sound, passing by the front of our house.

"Namo"

Matching the sound of tapping the wooden fish, "Ta Ta" sound, so slowly, slowly, spitting out a desolate and exuberant voice, after this sound dissipated in the morning air, the dawn had already penetrated through the clam shell window.

This, in my mood, is really no less than a kind of heavy oppression. I was afraid of hearing such a simple and sad tone. Curling up in bed. I would have to wait until the sunlight had combed through the curtains and spread to the front of the bed before daring to get up...

Once.

I woke up in the gurgling sound of rain. That sad voice reciting the Buddha's name slowly passed under the window of the small building again.

"Namo 'Ta'"

At that time, I could not suppress the exuberant mood aroused by this simple and sincere tone. I pushed open the window... The gray shadow of the unkempt-haired ascetic monk dissolved in the fine rain threads was hazy. A wisp of faint blue smoke rose from the statue of Wei Tuo he was carrying on his back, curling up.

"Namo Amitabha!"

He recited the Buddha's name so devotedly, and at the places where he paused, he bowed down and kowtowed his head on the slate.

I waited until that hazy shadow disappeared at the entrance of the alley, and that sobbing tone still lingered and weaved in the sound of the rain. I don't know why, but since that time, I have developed a kind of intimate liking for that lonely outsider and that desolate voice reciting the Buddha's name and tone.

Because, we are both unfortunate people drifting on the horizon!

Bivalve Shells Producing Arhats 211

— Chen Zizhan

This is truly a strange occurrence: Arhats growing on bivalve shells. Not five hundred, not even eighteen, but nineteen.

This strange occurrence seems to be absolutely true.

The day before yesterday (September 28th), the Xinwen Bao newspaper published "The Strange Tale of Bivalves Producing Arhats." It stated that Tong Shuangxi, a farmer from Fangxian Bridge in the city of Shaoxing, went to work in the fields a few days ago. By chance, he caught a bivalve in a small pond. Its shell was as soft as cotton. Unexpectedly, within a few minutes of being taken out of the soil, the shell hardened, becoming like an ordinary bivalve, and nineteen Arhats appeared on the shell. This caused a sensation, and countless people, near and far, came to see it. Some even offered to buy it for a thousand yuan. Currently, Tong Shuangxi has brought this bivalve shell to Shanghai, hoping to sell it for a good price. The Shanghai Yu Ji Photo Studio, located at 498 East Huade Road, submitted a photograph of the Arhats on the bivalve shell to the Xinwen Bao for printing. However, the photograph is not clear, and I cannot accurately discern the true appearance of these nineteen Arhats.

Many curious people in Shanghai believe that the bivalve shell Arhats will surely be bought and displayed in an amusement park, just like the "crab shell beauties" of previous years.

Why would Arhats grow on bivalve shells?

If this is indeed the case, we must hope that eminent biologists or zoologists will provide us with an explanation, if they are able to do so.

Strangely enough, bivalve shells producing Arhats is not unprecedented. Moreover, this strange occurrence happened in Zhejiang, but not in Shaoxing, but in Hangzhou. In Yang Yu's "Shanju Xinhua," there is the following record:

Emperor Wenzong enjoyed eating clams. Among them, there were some broken and unseparated ones. The emperor burned incense and prayed for them. After a short while, they opened on their own. Inside were snail-like ornaments, with clothing and lotus leaves, which were called Bodhisattvas. The emperor placed them in a box made of golden sandalwood and bestowed them upon a benevolent temple, ordering them to be treated with respect. I saw two bivalve shells in the home of an old family in Hangzhou. Inside were eighteen Arhats, all meticulously prepared. Later, they were given to the left prime minister Dali Ma Si. To seek the reason behind this is not something that can be forced or misinterpreted.

In this light, bivalve shells producing Arhats seems to be a real occurrence. Yang Yu also mentions Emperor Wenzong eating clams, and finding Buddhas and Bodhisattvas inside the clam shells, which is also a strange thing. Yang Yu lived in the late Yuan Dynasty. The Wenzong he mentions doesn't specify the dynasty, so it seems to be Yuan Wenzong. I wonder if this is correct. The Fudeng Lu states that Emperor Wenzong of the Tang Dynasty also liked to eat clams and once saw a Buddha statue inside a clam shell. In short, Bodhisattvas appearing inside clam shells also seems to be a real occurrence.

I recall that not long ago, I saw many sideshows at a festive welcoming ceremony in Jiangwan, and then came a bivalve shell beauty. A friend hurriedly called out to me:

"Look, a bivalve shell spirit!"

"(No, a bivalve shell Guanyin.)" I smiled.

"(Don't profane the divine!)" He also smiled.

"(The bivalve shell Guanyin has a classic origin)," I said.

"(What classic origin?)" He asked me.

"(It comes from a notebook written by a person from the Song Dynasty……)"

I am not fabricating rumors. Originally, there is a passage about Guanyin in a bivalve shell in Hong Mai's "Yijian Zhi":

Yu Ji, a resident of Piaoshui, went to Taizhou Xinghua as a Lieutenant during the Xuanhe era, traveling by boat with his family. There were many bivalves in the Huai River, and the boatmen often ate them. Whenever Yu Ji saw them, he would buy them and release them into the river. One day, he obtained a basket that was very heavy. The people wanted to eat them, offering twice the price, but he firmly refused and placed them in a pot. Suddenly, a loud noise arose from the pot, accompanied by bright flames, filling the boat with great fear. After eating them, a large bivalve split open, revealing an image of Avalokiteśvara in the shell, with two bamboo stalks standing upright as if alive beside her. The Bodhisattva's appearance was beautiful and dignified, with a crown, clothing, and ornaments made of fine pearls. The bamboo leaves, branches, and stems were also made of fine pearls. Yu Ji ordered everyone on the boat to recite Buddhist scriptures and repent of their sins, and he took the shell home.

Truly strange, Arhats growing on bivalve shells, Guanyin sitting inside bivalve shells. The former is something that can be investigated and observed right now, while the latter is based solely on an ancient record. If neither of these stories are lies, then eminent biologists or zoologists will surely have a reasonable explanation. However, even if there are places that look like human faces, scientists will not admit that these are Arhats and that is Guanyin.

Random Notes from the Universe (4) 212

— Ling Mo

The most superficial thing about mankind's understanding and naming of the bright moon is that lunar eclipses can be calculated accurately. If the moon's path were not drifting, then there would be a lunar eclipse every month at opposition. Because of the drifting, lunar eclipses are not very frequent. Similarly, because of the drifting, there are very few times when the sun and moon are in opposition at exactly 0 degrees. This year's Mid-Autumn Festival is considered to be very close, and it is indeed rare because this first requires the vernal or autumnal equinox to occur on the day of the full moon. (It is even rarer for them to occur at the same time; I remember seeing a lunar eclipse during the Mid-Autumn Festival, which probably coincided with the autumnal equinox, but I cannot verify this at the moment.) What makes us most directly interested is being able to see which longitude the moon is at and which star it is in conjunction with when the autumnal equinox meets the full moon. Unfortunately, this time the moon is precisely full during the daytime, so we cannot see it. However, when the moon rises at dusk on that day, the moon will have just passed 0 hours of right ascension, and the sun will not yet have reached 12 hours of right ascension. The full moon and the setting sun will be in the sky at the same time, facing each other in the east and west, which is also a spectacular sight. Many people probably noticed this, but fewer probably noticed that the sky seen at this time is exactly from 180 degrees west to 360 degrees east.

Both 180 degrees and 360 degrees are intersection points of the ecliptic and celestial equator. When the ecliptic crosses the sky symmetrically from east to west, the winter solstice point is at the zenith, in the constellation Sagittarius. We can directly observe this phenomenon by recognizing the constellation Sagittarius at the zenith. For those who don't recognize the stars, this is the most convenient opportunity to recognize the stars of the ecliptic. An old-style calendar still attempts to indicate the position of the sun, moon, and stars, but new-style calendars almost completely lack this. Although modern calendars focus more on human affairs and less on celestial phenomena, it will be impossible to determine the calendar completely without celestial phenomena in the near future. The time on present-day clocks is still based on celestial phenomena.

The autumnal and vernal equinoxes are roughly the standard by which our clocks measure a day of 24 hours. It is on these two days that the day and night are approximately 12 hours each. In addition, not only is the length of time from sunrise to sunset different from the length of time from sunset to sunrise, but the time from one sunrise to the next is also not exactly 24 hours. Calculating how many full 24-hour days each person can live will inevitably make one feel the brevity of life.

The system of dividing a day into 24 hours is now worldwide. I don't know if it will change in the future. But it is really not very convenient because it does not match the 360 degrees of a circle. Now, astronomical right ascension of 360 degrees has been changed to time longitude to accommodate clocks, but it would actually be more convenient to change man-made clocks to accommodate 360 degrees. The reason for not doing so is probably because clocks are used by most people every day, while time longitude is more specialized and used less. However, it is precisely because of this gap that astronomical knowledge is not easily popularized.

If I continue to discuss this, I will have to go from the universe to the cosmos, so I will stop here for now.

Mr. Village Chief (18) 214

— Wang Renshu

(I ran and ran to this house, this woman always said her husband had gone up up up the mountain. I ran and ran to that house, that woman always said her husband had gone down down down to the fields. So, my running was all in vain, so every night night night I would go to the village entrance to circle. Meeting this one, this one carrying a load of rice seedlings, coming from the mountain. (Damn it, are you here to take my life?) They always cursed like that. (Your father's fields, these past few years the price of rice husks has been cheap, your father is so poor he didn't even put down any seeds last year, but this year we still have to plant, we can only cut bark · tender trees · as rice seedlings. One mu of land needs ten loads, your father only plants five mu of land, so it's enough to be tired for a whole spring. What free time do we have to learn drills. Meeting that one, that one again carrying a load of cow manure to the fields. (You eat it and you're really happy.) They also said it with so so so much sorrow. (Where can we get a free hand. You see last year, there was no money in our fields to put down soybean cakes, and the seeds we did put down didn't sprout. But those two wild children from Huang Liu's family, with nothing to eat, every day they come to my Hengdong Three Stone to steal seeds, to fill up their mother's belly… There's also also also that that lame Dong Sheng said, looking at Mr. Dasheng, that whose cows, also take advantage of their power power power… and ate half a qiu of our field. We don't even have time to spread cow manure. But to farm, you always have to swallow your anger! If it was really someone from the family, and we could just let them starve to death, then I would go be a soldier and eat state rations, happy by my——myself…)… You think, if he he they say so so so much, what way can I think?)

(So good, so good. I won't manage it anymore.) Mr. Dasheng jumped up. (Awen, although he is the village chief, the village chief is an unpaid position. He doesn't eat from the government, and doesn't suffer government troubles. Squad leader, you can do as you please, just grab one at the village entrance to fill the position!)

Mr. Feng Wen had been running around for half the day, and had finally caught up with the squad leaders' rice and vegetables. He shuffled in.

(Good, Awen, go tell the people in the village that you're not managing this matter anymore. Tell lame Dongsheng to spread the word. Go, go! Say that I said it.) Mr. Dasheng waved his hand angrily. Lame Dongsheng pouted and went out. But once he walked down the street, he felt like the world was his again. He shouted at the top of his lungs, (You're not going! See if you're not going! It's an order from above, you dare disobey! Hmph!)

Mr. Dasheng watched lame Dongsheng go out. Then he leaned in and whispered to Village Chief Feng Wen. (If we're grabbing people, of course, it can only be Shanfu and Chuncai. They don't farm. They're idle at home, and they still smoke that. (Saying that, he raised his little and thumb as if holding a tobacco pipe.) Second, there's Aji, but Azhao has gone, Aji, don't let them grab him.)

However, opening to the far term, because the silver money gangs heard that they were active again, the buying intention was very strong, so the market price only fell 3 or 4 fen, and there was little huge fluctuation. Therefore, the subsequent rounds gradually rebounded. This month, the factory slightly made up for the rebound, especially Lian. By the time the afternoon market opened, trading had turned light, and the market atmosphere had turned calm. Because the exchange, in view of the excessive decline, was too risky, from now on, all buying and selling security deposits will be changed to 500 yuan. This situation is tantamount to restricting speculative activities, so the transaction is less, and the market is also stable. As a result, this month rebounded 7 fen from the previous opening, still down 1 fen before the market closed, November fell 1 fen and 2.5 li, December fell 1 fen and a half, January and February did not move, and March was still postponed.

Chronicles

Xiao Xi Tian (Little Western Heaven) 229

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Two: Making a Fortune and Entering the Folk Road, Returning to Yongshou, Bidding Farewell to Family, Coming to the Heavens, People Arriving in Chang'an

Jia Duocai smiled and said, "I guessed it right away. You must have gone to the Tobacco Tax Bureau to see the director. Did you see him?" Li Shilian said, "You underestimate me. Besides him, I don't make friends with others?" Early this morning, Director Wu sent his own car to the door of the hotel to take me to visit Zhouling. Originally, he wanted to send me off himself, but a public affair happened temporarily, so he had to send his most popular person, Section Chief Chang, who is also a secretary, to go with him. When crossing Xianyang Ancient Ferry, we got on the boat, and others got off the boat. I saw such a girl. Actually, she's not a child, about sixteen or seventeen years old." Jia Duocai put down his chopsticks, looked at him, and asked, "Is that floral jacket a large hibiscus?" Li Shilian said, "How can I see it so realistically? But a large flower is good." Jia Duocai said, "Is it an oval face, with a chin that is not very sharp?" Li Shilian said, "Yes, you're here, they're here too, you go find them." At that time, the two people were talking happily, and unknowingly ate up the two pots of wine in front of them. According to Jia Duocai's excitement, he had to ask for another pot of wine, but Li Shilian said, "I'm afraid Section Chief Chang will come to talk later, so I dare not get drunk." Only then did he stop the wine, and each ate. After the meal, I returned to Little Western Heaven, and it was already dark. Walking to the center of the street, on that straight tree pole, hung an oil lamp as big as a vegetable bowl, and the wick was burning and roaring. Li Shilian said, "Xi'an is such a big city, and there is no electricity yet. This is really a shortcoming." As he was saying this, he heard a very delicate voice coming to his ears, "Look, look, there's another one here. This lamp is so bright that if a needle falls on the ground, you can pick it up." Looking, the person who said this was an oval-faced girl wearing a floral jacket. (32)

Apricot Spring Bridge Moon String 230

— Nanguongsheng

On the eighteenth day of August, Suzhou has the grand event of the Apricot Spring Bridge Moon String in Stone Lake. According to legend, on the morning of this day, it is the seventeenth night. The bright moon in the sky seen on the Apricot Spring Bridge in Stone Lake can be reflected in the lake, forming a string, as if there are many bright moons appearing in the sky. For what reason, I can't tell you why, but going to Stone Lake to see the Apricot Spring Bridge Moon String on August 18 has become the purpose of Suzhou people's entertainment, and all the engraved articles over the years.

One side of Stone Lake is Shangfang Mountain. There is nothing on the mountain except a Wutong Temple, which is actually a deserted mountain. The Wutong was very magical in the former Qing Dynasty, so I don't know how many people went to the mountain to burn incense, especially on the eighteenth day. On this day, the witches in the villages along the mountain and in the city borrowed this to call out. On this day, they wore white skirts and white clothes, running from the mountain to the foot of the mountain, and from the foot of the mountain to the top of the mountain, which is called jumping witch, falsely saying that there is a god protecting them and attaching to their bodies, deceiving the foolish women who burn incense. After Su Fu Tang Wenzheng drove out the Wutong God, the magic of the Wutong God was gone, but those witches still jumped their witches on this day, which can be regarded as a scene of the Apricot Spring Bridge Moon String. In the past, there were many ships from all directions to Chaosan in Stone Lake, selling boxing, burning incense, walking rope, doing business, plus Suzhou people to Taihu Lake to play flower boats and painted boats, countless, crowded a small Stone Lake, and they were full of flower lanterns, banquets opened grapes, Shengge all night, scholars and women like clouds, it is a rare grand meeting.

Tidbits 231

— (Du Juan)

General Deng Tiemei, the leader of the Northeast Volunteer Army, was executed on the night of September 28 in the Republic of China. It is a natural result that General Deng sought benevolence and got benevolence. Have you ever seen Yue Fei and Wen Tianxiang surrender to the enemy? I hope that the people of the country will remember this day, September 28, as deeply as September 18 in their hearts, and prepare to move forward one day, stepping on the blood of General Deng, and avenge General Deng.

How to Develop the Northwest? 232

— Ziwei

(Developing the Northwest,) Since this slogan was shouted out by the general public, almost some people have paid considerable attention to it; knowing that it is not a matter of empty talk, but relies entirely on the efforts of practical work.

How can the Northwest be developed? This is naturally a question that expects to be answered.

In fact, the Northwest has been suffering from drought for years. Farmers are always shouting about drought all year round. People who live in famine are already very satisfied if they can hope to avoid starvation. It is simply equal to whipping a critically ill camel to ask them to share their strength from themselves to develop their own treasures, and calling it to carry heavy loads on a vague and unknowable journey. It is indeed extremely difficult.

Therefore, the major and difficult task of developing the Northwest does not only rely on their own willingness to seek development, but also relies on various assistance from other aspects.

We know that the amount of water in the Northwest, such as Shaanxi and Gansu, is extremely scarce, and farmers naturally feel extremely difficult to cultivate. We will leave aside the problem of developing the rich resources of the Northwest for the time being. However, the preliminary basic work is still how to build canals and how to facilitate the communication of waterways.

Everything must start from construction, so that the rich treasures of the Northwest can rely on scientific methods to complete its initial attempt to develop. This advocacy theory is naturally considered by the general public to be the most appropriate and excellent method. Like the movie (Go to the Northwest) being staged in Xinguang these days, it also provides a very obvious point for this, and I hope everyone will give the same enthusiastic promotion and support, and develop the actual treasures of our barren Northwest into the only rich source of our Northwest.

Expecting that all practical workers will complete this great wish and work hard to develop the rich treasures of our Northwest.

Records of Fleeting Fragrance from the Imperial Incense 233

— Originally Written by Princess Der Ling of Qing, Translated by Qin Shouou

Confucius is the most remarkable figure in Chinese history. Anyone who has read a little knows something of his deeds. The Empress Dowager also absolutely worshiped this old master. She also memorized many of Confucius’s words. Whenever she reviewed memorials or taught her subordinates, she often liked to quote a few sentences, seemingly to increase the confidence of those who read or heard them.

The above two paragraphs were brought to mind because I wrote about the Empress Dowager humming Li Bai’s poem "Spring Dawn" in the carriage, and it has little to do with this chapter of the book. Now let us stop there.

In retrospect, this trip to the Northeast was not an arduous long journey for the Empress Dowager, but it was still very hard for an elderly person accustomed to a pampered life! However, at that time, she herself did not feel it. This was because she was stimulated by a kind of excitement in her heart, and she only wanted to return to the homeland of her own ancestors! Yehe Nara (the Empress Dowager's mother's surname), to the old garden where she grew up (which is also where the author's ancestors grew up), so her spirit was particularly invigorated, and she easily overcame the fatigue she suffered physically. During the heyday of the Qing Dynasty, Emperor Qianlong once returned to Fengtian, but apart from this heroic and promising emperor, the Empress Dowager was the first among the emperors and empresses of the Qing Dynasty to return to her hometown. I think she must have had extremely warm expectations for the various scenes of her hometown.

The day after we passed Tianjin, the train gradually approached the world-famous Shanhaiguan. (142)

▲ P.S. Yesterday, I received a message from Mr. Yi: According to the Qing system, only banner officials could refer to themselves as "slave," so when Yuan Shikai met the Empress Dowager Cixi, he used "your subject." I hereby correct this and thank Duke Yi.

Extraordinary Woman 234

— Hua Ling

A new family has moved into our tenement building. The head of the family is nearly sixty years old and surnamed Wu, but his wife is only about twenty-five or twenty-six years old.

After a week, we became familiar with each other, and we chatted. I discovered in our conversations that Mrs. Wu was an extraordinary woman.

According to her, she left the customs at the age of sixteen. Her husband died within a year. Two months later, she had a relationship with a man she was living with, so she broke away from her husband's family and went outside to start a family. After living together for half a year, they separated due to disagreements. Then, she fell in love with an employee of a certain company out of friendship and got married formally. A year later, she suddenly discovered that her husband was already married, so she broke free again. Several months later, she became inextricably linked with a certain comprador. This time, she was openly a concubine. However, after living together for a year, she felt that although the comprador spent money freely, his temper was too bad and it was really not easy to please him, so they both agreed to separate. Later, she encountered a certain military officer, and they became devoted to each other. Then, she followed her husband, traveling all over the country for more than two years, and their relationship was very good. But unfortunately, he was injured and died in a certain war. So she came back and married a clerk from a silk shop and became a formal couple. This silk shop clerk was born with a gambling habit and often gambled all night without returning. After several quarrels, she had to seek another way out. Last year, she married Mr. Wu as a concubine. Mr. Wu is the manager of a tea shop.

Miscellaneous Talk

Random Notes on National Martial Arts 235

— Shi Cheng

In Chinese martial arts, Shaolin is the most respected. Branches and factions have multiplied, and the true essence has gradually been lost. Wudang rose up, competing for dominance. Its schools are divided into internal and external, excluding dissidents, and factions fighting each other like fire and water, which has been criticized by the world. Wudang is an internal school. Its practice lies in preserving the spirit and breath, and strengthening the internal organs. Therefore, Tai Chi boxing emphasizes intention rather than strength. Shaolin is an external school. Its purpose is to forge muscles and bones and strengthen the body. Therefore, tiger, leopard, crane, snake, ape and other boxing styles all emphasize agility, strength and might. The methods are different, and the paths are naturally different. The external school despises the internal school as unable to withstand a single blow, and the internal school mocks the external school as an iron cabinet containing porcelain. (Because their leg muscles are hard as iron, while the internal organs in their abdomens are as fragile as porcelain.) They each consider themselves superior and despise each other. In fact, there are many internal schools in Shaolin, which cannot be generalized; and there are also many outstanding people in the external schools. Which is inferior and which is superior depends on the depth of their skills, and cannot be judged by school or faction.

Shaolin boxing began with Bodhidharma. Bodhidharma was the first patriarch of Zen Buddhism in the East. After failing to achieve his goals with Emperor Wu of Liang, he retired to Mount Song and faced the wall in Shaoshi Temple. Although he realized his original nature and saw his true nature, he sat motionless for nine years, and his legs were ruined. Therefore, he used the method of clenching his fists with both hands to forge his muscles and bones. After accumulating merit for a long time, the muscles could be moved when he clenched his fists, from the arm to the shoulder, to the neck, to the chest and back, to the abdomen, to the arms, gradually to the thighs, legs, and even the heels. His legs were able to return to their original state, and he could move as usual. The world only knows that the Yijin Jing and Xisui Jing are the supreme secrets of the Shaolin school! The Xisui Jing will not be discussed for the time being, but the above-mentioned method of clenching the fists is the first twelve sections of the Yijin Jing. (The Yijin Jing published in recent bookstores is not without discrepancies with the true teachings. The true kung fu is plain and unremarkable, while the published versions are not without showing off strangeness and flaunting wonders.)

The Wudang school was founded by Zhang Sanfeng in the early Ming Dynasty. Sanfeng was a Taoist priest. Taoist cultivation takes condensing the spirit and refining the Qi as the first priority. The so-called refining elixir is their terminology. Therefore, Taoist priests are also called refiners or complete truths. Refining means refining Qi; complete truth means completing their truth. (Excluding those who specialize in catching demons and worshiping repentances, who were under the jurisdiction of Zhang Tianshi of Longhu Mountain before the Republic of China.) The method began with the medical school's "Su Wen" and "Ling Shu"; originated from the ancient guiding techniques; Chisong and Zijing both have special books, and Hua Tuo's Five Animal Frolics is its variation. Chen Xiyi of the Song Dynasty wrote "Twenty-Four Qi Healing Sitting Exercises," which is even more refined. Sanfeng integrated guiding, refining Qi, Shaolin martial arts and other techniques into one furnace; integrating and connecting them, he achieved this unique skill. Therefore, his superior kung fu is still in refining essence, refining Qi, and refining spirit. Tai Chi boxing is only used to exercise the body, making it lively, relaxing muscles, and smoothing the flow of Qi and blood! The secrets of Wudang are not exhausted here.

There are many martial artists in Pudong, all descendants of Shaolin. Leaving aside those whose attainments are profound but whose names are unknown, according to what I have heard, Qin Heqi, Xu Xifan, and Gu Yuanxiu were all famous figures of their time. Now Qin and Xu have both passed away, and among the younger generation, only Gu Yuanxiu is like a rare surviving fruit.

Qin Jun Heqi was a friend of mine despite the age gap. His ancestors were originally from Shandong. His ninth ancestor, Gong Haichuan, was a disciple of Gong Lin. He moved to Pudong. Jun inherited his family learning and attained great depths. He practiced internal family boxing in the Shaolin school. His family business was traumatology, and his circle of friends was wide. He was a good friend of Huo Yuanjia, whose name shook the country. During the Shanghai National Martial Arts Examination, he served as the director of traumatology rescue. The unsavory stories about his life have been used as materials for "Biographies of Modern Knights and Heroes." Therefore, they have been popular for a long time and will not be repeated. Novelists may have exaggerated and embellished them, but the records are all facts and not castles in the air.

Xu and Gu were strangers to me at first, and I only knew that they were masters of national martial arts. My friend Jin told me anecdotes about the two gentlemen, one for each, which are recorded below:

Xu Jun had an argument with his two nephews over something. The nephews were also strong and wanted to make trouble for him. Jun lightly grasped their arms and dragged them, and the nephews could not stop. Then he released them and smiled and said: (Young people, don't be so aggressive!) The sleeves of the nephews' short shirts made of homespun suddenly fell off. Taking them and looking at them, the breaks were like knife cuts. The place where he grabbed them was Jun's grip. But the sleeves of the long shirts outside were completely unharmed, and the skin was not injured at all. What amazing skill!

Gu Jun once lived in the home of lawyer Ma Youren. Several strong men thought of testing his skills. So they placed two rope circles on the ground. Gu went to urinate and stepped into the circles with both feet. The strong men suddenly came out and dragged them, but the ropes broke and Gu stood still without moving. His foot strength was also amazing.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

Desire for Fame 236

— Chen Liang

I have heard people say that fame is a person's second life. People have a desire to live, so people also have a desire for fame.

Regarding the desire for fame, I should have quoted a few classics, but because I have no research in archeology, I dare not talk nonsense. I might as well talk about reality frankly.

Fame is abstract, like air, like wind, like vocal cords. Its ability to spread is very wide and fast. If you have a reputation in place A, place B and place C will know it in a short time, and then it will spread to the whole county, the whole province, and even the whole world. The so-called (sound vibrates the universe) (famous all over the world) is just that.

Of course, fame is like money. It cannot be obtained by sitting idly. (Seeking fame) means that you have to (seek) it to get it. However, empty seeking is also useless. Otherwise, stealing fame will ultimately be harmful to hearing, and it is not wise to lose one's personality in the pursuit of fame. People who are full all day and do nothing, even if they have a belly full of desire for fame, are also futile. Cooking rice without rice will never produce rice. Fishing without bait will never catch fish. (Behavior) is the bait for catching (fame), which is a matter of course.

Or someone might say, (behavior) seems too general. What kind of (behavior) can catch fame? In fact, this is not a problem. For example, earthworms and red-headed flies can catch fish. (Behavior) can naturally be casual. As the saying goes: (If you can't be famous for a hundred generations, you should be notorious for ten thousand years.) As long as everyone knows that there is such a remarkable figure, that is enough. Good or bad is of course another question. Fragrant is fame, and smelly is also fame.

For example, if you can't save the country, or you don't dare to save the country, then you have to try the means of selling out the country and destroying the country, such as Zheng Xiaoxu and Xi Qia. Although you are indeed guilty in your conscience, you will not attract people's attention if you don't do this. At that time, if someone is scolding, opposing, or even wanting to treat you to a bomb, you don't have to be afraid, and you can't change your attitude. You should understand that at this time, your fame is spreading widely, in newspapers, on walls, and in toilets. Your great name is found everywhere, from domestic to foreign, and the whole world is paying attention. This is the total harvest period of fame.

Rainy Day 237

— Yun Yi

I really like rainy days. This is my subjective preference, and there is no great significance. I can neither accompany my lover inside a glass window hung with tassels, smoking cigars and enjoying the rain, nor do I have the poetic exuberance of a poet to write poems praising the rain scene; yet I always like rainy days. There was a time when a friend and I were unemployed and living in Shanghai West. We couldn't go out during the day, and we felt even more terrible at night. Fortunately, the window of our small building faced the street. Every day, the two of us leaned on the window sill to look at the window decorations across the street, the cars and trams in the road, and the flower girls on the sidewalk. But later, we were able to close our eyes and clearly imagine these objects, so we hoped for a rainy day to adjust our mental pain. In fact, unemployed people seem to have been deprived of the right to live, and rainy days for us are just the two of us leaning on the window sill to look at the window decorations across the street, the cars and trams in the road, and the flower girls on the sidewalk, but the fine raindrops are really too beautiful a background. However, I cannot describe the beauty of this rainy day. Even if I collect many nice words to describe it, they are still inadequate. Moreover, I think there are many like-minded people among readers. The benefits of this rainy day are only experienced by like-minded people. If others feel disgusted by rainy days, then what I write will be futile.

These days, it has been raining consistently again. Although I am relatively more employed now, I still have a stubborn fondness for rainy days. My office is on the fifth floor of a tall Western-style building. Although my position is also good, it is by the window. However, the best thing is that there are no equally tall Western-style buildings opposite. As far as I can see, I seem to have changed my environment. According to my years of experience in the city, there is certainly no such sublimity, and it is floating with the sudden big and small rain. I seem to be sleepwalking to an unknown scenic spot. In this way, I am often stunned and forget to work.

For the past few days, I have been completely immersed in the beautiful scenery of the rain. I also sat stupidly for two hours on that day off. It is also raining today. When I was holding a pen and thinking blankly, I suddenly felt an unhappy thought, but I couldn't say why. In short, the rain today seems to have lost its inherent beauty. It cannot move my hobby as it used to. However, my love for rainy days will not change.

I thought of the friend who watched the rain with me. A month after I grabbed this job, he was urged to return home by a family letter. On the day of parting, it was such a rainy day. He brought a box of broken books, and I had a burst of hot tears. The two of us separated. Later, he wrote in a letter that he faked the letter to leave because he didn't want to rely on me. He hoped that I would work hard and that we would meet again.

In this way, it has been two years, and there is no news from him. I wonder if he is also watching the rain today... does he also think of and miss his old friend?

I really hope that tomorrow will be a sunny day, otherwise, that unhappy thought will entangle my heart like a snake!

But what is that sound hitting the glass window? I bury my head and dare not look up.

Modern Husband Westernized Servant 238

Wild Children 239

— Yi

The autumn wind brought coolness, and the rain was drizzling. There were very few pedestrians on the road, only these few wild children were still wandering in the streets late at night.

(Hey! Where did that kid Xiaomao go?)

Xiao San tightened his pace, approached Ah Yun, and asked in a low voice.

(God knows. That guy Xiaomao has been caught again.)

As soon as Ah Yun finished speaking, everyone laughed. Xiao Heizi said with a smile:

(Xiaomao has been unlucky these past few days. Ah San has come to)

(Make trouble with him.)

The street lights in the deep night looked particularly dim and yellow. The sky was dark and stuffy, like a lead plate pressing down tightly. The few wild children, shrinking their heads and necks, walked further and further away.

At this time, Xiaomao was still squatting alone under the shop porch of a cigarette paper shop in an alley, shrinking his head. The thin and tattered summer cloth shirt on his body was soaked through by the rain and clung tightly to his skin. It was already a bit cool in the autumn night, and he was wearing this dripping shirt, which made the pores on Xiaomao's body stand up one by one, and he shivered more and more coldly.

For the past few days, Xiaomao's luck has been really bad. He couldn't do the business of pulling a cart on the North Sichuan Road Bridge, and the dozens of copper coins he used to sell evening newspapers were all eaten up, so he couldn't even sell the newspapers. Yesterday, he was caught and slapped in the face for nothing. He hasn't had any rice in his stomach for a whole day today, and it just so happened to start raining. In short, Xiaomao's situation of bad luck these past few days was the first time he had encountered it.

At this time, his stomach was full of sullenness, but he couldn't think of a way.

(Isn't that Xiaomao?)

Page 20

Several people walked over from that dark place, and one of them shouted loudly. Xiaomao heard it was Xiao Heizi's voice, so he clapped his hands twice in response.

(You guy, I've been looking for you for a long time. Hurry up, there's a business deal over there!)

At this time, Xiaomao was staring blankly at the ground at the few of them. He didn't even bother to listen to Xiao Heizi's words.

(Hey, what are you eating? I'm starving to death. Give me some!)

(Ha, so you're starving. There's plenty to eat, I'm afraid your little belly can't hold it.)

Xiao Heizi said jokingly, but Xiaomao heard that there was something to eat, and his body didn't tremble anymore. He jumped up and grabbed Xiao Heizi.

(Tell me quickly, where is there something to eat? I'll go, I'm really starving to death.)

On the quiet road, Xiaomao and them were walking. Looking at them walking to the corner of Peng Road, Xiao San clapped his hands twice to notify them.

Xiaomao hurried a few steps, approached Xiao San, and grabbed Xiao San with one hand again.

(Hey, what is there to eat? Take it out quickly.)

(There's plenty. If we do the business, we can even buy a new set of clothes to wear.)

(What kind of good business is that? I'll go do it, tell me quickly.)

A group of five or six of them squatted in the dark place at the corner of the road, talking in low voices for a long time. Everyone seemed very happy, and they ran around in the drizzle on the road.

But it is said that Xiaomao and his few wandering friends spent this cold and hungry autumn rainy night living behind iron bars. Their crimes were that they did not engage in proper occupations and repeatedly committed thefts.

Since that night, the North Sichuan Road area has reduced a few wild children wandering in the streets.

Miscellaneous Feelings from the Autumn Window, No. 3 240

— Jun

Nostalgia

The traces of autumn linger on the late-ripening grape clusters... linger on the late-blooming chrysanthemum bushes. Chrysanthemums are covered with red gold petals, chrysanthemums are covered with purple gold petals, lying in the warm sunshine, facing the warm sunshine and smiling lightly. Right next to the frame covered with colorful chrysanthemums, I smell the faint fragrance of chrysanthemums and start daydreaming.

In my dream, I deeply taste the aftertaste of lips as sweet as grapes, and listen to private love songs pouring out of a clear throat, pouring out the secrets of young Linlin's heart. Linlin's heart is a secret. Linlin is really a lovable and worrying white swallow! Swallows change with the change of seasons.

Linlin stretched out her hand to pick a red grape and squinted her eyes and said:

Late-blooming grapes have a late-blooming secret taste, the symbol of love!

I chew the secret taste of grapes and the taste of love with the secret taste of grapes! These days, my whole heart, my thoughts, are all resting on Linlin's grape-flavored lips and hair.

A heart immersed in the confusion of love, joyful and worried.

Autumn is the season for falling leaves, and the color of my love has also peeled off the brilliant color.

Swallows change their homes with the change of seasons.

Linlin has indeed become a swallow of the season!

Swallow-like Linlin, where are you flying now? Although there are still grape clusters and chrysanthemum gold petals in her old home, there is no longer the light shadow of Linlin, like a swallow. In the misty drizzle, her old home is shrouded in the deep loneliness of autumn. Lonely old home.

But the old home has had a time when it was not lonely.

But Linlin, the swallow-like Linlin, has abandoned her old home to build her new home. But under the mountain frame are engraved the footprints of past hesitation and the footprints of love.

Linlin, do you have time to recall the past? Will you fly back like a swallow at this time next year?

The heart of Linlin, like a swallow, is as unpredictable as the season of May!

With the rising autumn wind, Linlin suddenly floated south. With one heart. Leaving me behind, but my whole heart, my whole soul, are still entangled in Linlin's grape-flavored lips and hair. I want to wait for Linlin to return to my side, to hear her light throat pour out private love songs, pour out the secrets of young Linlin's heart. Waiting for a longer time.

But I don't know if Linlin will come back after all?

I also understand that all banquets must end, and the past scenes cannot be chased back, just as the raindrops that fall on the ground cannot be called to fly back to the sky. Only because the emotion Linlin gave me was too intense, my whole life was greatly shaken, and I couldn't calm down no matter what.

Every day, from morning to night, I stand in front of the window like a lost soul, looking at the green sky. Waiting for Linlin, like a swallow, to fly down from the sky.

With my twenty-one years of depressed heart.

But when will Linlin come back? Will she come back?

Bowing in Distress 241

— Yun Zhi

(The poor are overly harsh, they look at the world with different eyes.)

— Dostoevsky, "The Poor")

In the morning, I wiped my hazy eyes with a face cloth dipped in cold water, put on my old coat, and quickly reached into my outer pocket to count the remaining coins... one, two, three, four... I didn't dare to think too much. Today I have to live on less than ten copper coins.

When I went out, my eyes were hazy, and I carelessly discarded the happy dream, letting my consciousness be crushed by the iron wheels of reality, like a car crushing the road. I raised my head and looked at the straight chimneys on the top of the factory, the tram lines. When the tram passed by, the electric poles on the top of the car rubbed out green sparks at the joints of the lines, which flew and then disappeared silently.

(—The sparks of life's conflicts!)

Yes, the sparks of life's conflicts also explode and then disappear silently.

The copper coins in the bag started to sound again, and then my whole body started to tremble, a slight, empty, soft feeling. Experience flashed like lightning, is hunger! Hunger devouring people like a beast!

Thinking about it, it's ridiculous. Why does anyone need to know? In this world, the top knows, but people can't know people. If the world is a mystery, then although one may be disappointed in solving it, at least one can say that one has learned something from that soft feeling like a beast. People who have been hungry are not surprised at all by the abundant food placed in the display cabinets of food stores. When a person with an empty stomach keeps looking outside, he can't help but think... why can't I take it and eat it? Why is there a layer of glass in between? What is this layer of glass?

(And a thin layer of glass represents... a terrible force, human selfishness.)

The world is wearing a coat of glass.

And I feel that this layer of glass, it is powerful; it inherently contains an irrationality, a contradiction, a tragedy, the great tragedy of mankind.

Confused... then what does the world represent? Isn't it completely irrational?

It is not to say that a person who is starving is somewhat cruel, he has the courage to obliterate all the good intentions of (people); but this is not very justifiable, there are some people in the world who are as (ruthless) as iron, they treat suffering as a universal library, they learn everything from suffering, they look at the world with a different eye.

Looking at the crisscrossing buildings, looking at the clouds in the sky, looking at all the property that is less than ten copper coins, cruelly, calmly, and blankly.

The feeling is feverish, soft.

Novel

Uncle's Braid (22) 242

— Ling He

Dinner was ready. Xu Zhai's family was quite traditional, at least in the sense that men and women were separate; for example, the women could only eat in the kitchen, while in the main hall, the three brothers plus Shi Min each occupied a corner, making exactly four people.

Country life was usually very frugal. Except for the first and fifteenth of the month, there was rarely any meat on the table. Moreover, Old Master Zhengfu's family precepts were very strict, always emphasizing thrift. Today was already special because it was the second uncle's first day back home, so there was a bowl of fried eggs, which was already quite lavish; Shi Min knew this very well.

Zhi Zhai rarely spoke during meals. However, it wasn't that he didn't want to, but rather that he was preoccupied... regretting not writing a letter a couple of days earlier, so his wife didn't know he was back and was still enjoying herself at her parents' house. He would undoubtedly have to sleep alone tonight, and tomorrow morning, he would definitely visit his in-laws. But he was also worried that it might rain tomorrow; with tonight being so warm, the weather tomorrow was likely unreliable.

After a while, he had already eaten a bowl and a half of rice, and he remained silent, not saying a word. However, for some reason, the eldest and third brothers began to argue. He overheard them arguing about how remarkable and good Li Yuanhong's men were, while the eldest brother didn't think much of Li Yuanhong, arguing that since he had accepted the imperial salary, he should have been loyal to the country and shouldn't have joined the revolutionaries to start a rebellion. If he wasn't loyal to the Qing court, how could he be loyal to the Republic? As for Sun Wen and Huang Xing, they were a different matter because they didn't accept the imperial salary and devoted themselves to the revolution. Their greatness lay in this. Later, the eldest brother even presented evidence, saying...

"I won't talk about other things, just his recent proclamation... forbidding the private sheltering of officials, the infringement of commerce, and the killing of fellow countrymen, all of which are good. But he forbids harming foreigners and attacking foreign volunteer corps. How afraid of death is he!"

Opening (Lament of the Silkworm Woman) 245

Spring silkworms raised, autumn silkworms busy. Many young village women gather mulberry leaves. Farmers only seek to make ends meet. Farm women toil day and night, forgetting sleep and food. Lamps burn all night without rest. They eat only yellow rice, salted greens, and bean curd soup. Wet leaves are gathered and must be wiped dry. In the cold of spring, rice containers are filled. If a spring thunder sounds, the frightened silkworm woman worries and cries to heaven. Therefore, raising silkworms and making cocoons is not easy. It takes hard work and mental strain to fill their bellies. In recent years, Chinese silk merchants have suffered a blow. Mostly because of enemy countries' conspiracies and hidden arrows. It is hateful that unscrupulous silk merchants use artificial goods. Therefore, domestic silk has been harmed. It is hoped that the government will invent scientific instruments. To save sericulture, improvements are needed. Know that it is not too late to mend the fold after the sheep are lost. The silk merchants should rouse their spirits. Furthermore, I urge the national sericulture guidance centers. To persuade the farms to do their best to help. Manufacturing plants must strive for selection. Competing with silkworm cocoons can revitalize the country. Only then can Greater China's industry be forever boundless.

Radio Special News 247

The Shanghai Radio Drama Society, one of the most famous broadcasting drama troupes in Shanghai, has been established for several months. It has broadcast radio dramas on major radio stations in the city. The drama materials taken by the society are of pure and noble meaning, and most of them focus on the future of the nation and the survival of the country. Therefore, it has been warmly praised by the audience. In particular, the clear and fluent Mandarin dialogue of the members of the society is most praised. Shanghai Sound Film Company in this city has long admired its name, and specially sent personnel to discuss with Mr. Liu Hengzhi, the founder of the society, and invited Ms. Yan Fei, Xing Shu, and gentlemen such as Xu Jingsheng and Gao Mangsheng to produce sound films. It is heard that the consent of all has been obtained. From the first day of this month, the broadcast programs of each radio station will be temporarily suspended, and all the spirits will be devoted to the screen work. Once the film is completed, it will continue to be broadcast. Hope the audience pays attention.

Also, it is reported that Huaxing Radio Station in this city is scheduled to hold an opening ceremony on the 6th of this month. It specially invited the Shanghai Radio Drama Society to perform a special program. The society really could not refuse the kind invitation, and will broadcast the radio drama "Wu Song Kills His Sister-in-Law" on the radio station from 1 o'clock that night.
