Supplement to Shen Bao in this city Film Special

Physical Fitness on the Silver Screen 248

— Jia Bin

Driven by the trend of the times, although Chinese-made films have not yet reached the peak of artistic expression in form, they have been recognized as public education, and there are indeed many people who are vocally advocating cultural movements in films. Indeed, film always advances like a pioneer on the cultural foundation of a country. However, this mission cannot be shouldered by the numerous crudely made and shoddy film works. Frankly speaking, Chinese films still have a lot of bad and boring things. Not only do they lack content, but they also lack the skills of artistic expression. Talking about culture, isn't it an easy thing in Chinese films? But finally, someone has come out and has to do a cultural movement on this.

If film is truly film, I always acknowledge it as a pioneer of the times, symbolizing real life and promoting cultural evolution... In essence, it is not a tool of social education but a leader of social education. In form, it integrates various departments of art and strives to express (strength) and (beauty). (Strength) and (beauty) are not only indispensable basic conditions for film art, but also the most needed substance in the form and behavior of life. For example, we say that the more civilized the brain, the more barbaric the body. The so-called more barbaric body means that (strength) is its main component. As for (beauty), (modern beauty), health is essential for success.

Because of this, I have something I must say (physical fitness on the silver screen).

Physical fitness has indeed been a fashionable term in recent years. But in films, I have rarely seen anyone advocate this practical physical fitness movement. Perhaps some people will think of women's legs when they see the two words "physical fitness." In fact, what crime do their legs have! It's just that opinions differ.

It seems to be a common opinion many years ago... (The Lin Daiyu-style sickly beauty is no longer suitable as the (beauty) standard for Chinese women... Physical soundness is the standard of modern female beauty. Because according to the theory of eugenics, to restore the declining national strength, the health of motherhood is an urgent matter,) At that time, in fact, along with this argument, there were also various behaviors of women harming their own bodies in this contradictory society. The bad habit of breast binding has not been eradicated. Fortunately, the environment of life is constantly changing, perhaps because of the continuous advancement of culture, this bad habit will soon disappear without a trace. However, women's health is ultimately a slow process of progress. At present, there are still many women with Lin Daiyu-style sickly beauty parasitizing in society. Even if we sometimes see those deformed curves in the ballroom, although they don't bind their breasts, it is definitely not a manifestation of physical fitness. Moreover, they are very, very far from physical fitness. Because they are always too weak to withstand the wind.

Gentlemen who make films, I hope you pay correct attention to (physical fitness on the silver screen).

Film Review

Review of (The Soul of Beauty) — Central 249

— Ling He

It is said that this is an old work from a few years ago, but in general, it is a work worth watching.

However, strictly criticizing it, the director is using old methods to capture the audience due to the provisions of the script. Regarding this aspect, we can cite a point to explain the facts.

Xu Qinfang, feeling indignant due to the humiliation and the sadness of her father's death, jumps off a cliff to commit suicide. He Zhigang and Zheng Junli chase after her. On the mountain, in the forest, and by the cliff, it builds up to a climax. The appropriate and adequate editing makes this scene quite tense. However, the running back and forth and the fact that she is rescued just as she jumps down are inevitably very old-fashioned.

Another example is the last scene, the engagement of Xu Qinfang and He Zhigang. Xu Qinfang certainly does it very delicately, and the director's handling of the mood is also commendable. However, using Xu Qinfang's refusal to eat the pear that He Zhigang shared with her to show that she does not want to separate, and using two entangled velvet ropes to symbolize their love threads, is relatively difficult for most people to understand, and it is not a new method.

Of course, most of the above are the responsibility of the screenwriter. The director's full expression of what is contained in the play is naturally the minimum fulfillment of his own duty. However, a successful director should make up for the shortcomings of the script. For example, in the home of He Zhigang, the young master, since there is such a big house and such a big garden, why is there only one master and one servant? This is a shortcoming of the script, and the director should at least add a few more servants to make the family lively. Otherwise, this family is too exaggerated.

Indeed, the script has many shortcomings. Perhaps some people say that this script is at least very tortuous and bizarre. However, this is very far-fetched. If there were no chance encounters while eating in the Western restaurant, in the mountain house, and several times in the park, then this story simply could not have been strung together. (Why coincidences cannot be used in films does not need to be explained here.) It was enough for Xu Qinfang to suddenly cover for someone at Jiang Youyi's house, but it is simply impossible to justify her enduring humiliation at Shang Guanwu's house for the second time and stubbornly refusing to reveal his secret. Furthermore, in terms of the development of the characters' personalities, it is very inappropriate for Xu Qinfang to transform from a daughter guarding a tower to a modern girl. As for Gu Xiaohu going to Luoxing Street with a big black bow tie, how unreasonable is that? On the contrary, he said that Zheng Junli wearing a suit would easily attract the attention of the villains... These places should be the director's responsibility.

No, our review of the script does not stop there. More importantly, we must point out that if this is a detective film, then this story does not focus on the scientific solving of the detective case. On the contrary, if there were no several chance encounters, the case could not be revealed, and a lot of effort was made in other aspects. Therefore, rather than a detective film, it is better to say that it is an ordinary so-called love film.

As for the theme of the play, it is even more vague. Exposing the ugly state of the private lives of gentlemen is not the theme, so is it about plotting money and harming people? Then how ordinary and vulgar is that. The detective films produced by Warner, such as (New York Express), are worth learning from for playwrights.

The actors are all passable, but the makeup is slightly worse. Zhou Damin's photography is passable, at least the camera angles show effort.

An unprecedentedly great and tragic historical drama of the Mexican Revolution, the immortal work of Juarez Peel's life. (Long Live Freedom) One scene from within—Nanjing will screen it soon.

Audience Opinions

Postscript After Watching (Fragrant Snow Sea) 250

— Fu

(Fragrant Snow Sea) is indeed different from other films, with a unique and quiet interest. What is depicted inside is not the sin of the city, nor is it modern love, but a unique and pure folk sentiment, a real scene from a previous era, attacking the remnants of reality left over by the skillful technique. The novelty of its material and the depth of its meaning are indeed beyond ordinary imagination.

Regarding the selection of materials, the film takes the life of a village woman as the theme. She has gone through many hardships, joys and sorrows. Because she is deeply poisoned by superstition, she deeply believes that God is omnipotent, and asks God for all her difficulties. Coincidentally, superstition has given her everything, but also lost everything because after everything is fulfilled as she wishes, she fulfills her vow and becomes a nun. Of course, her heart is very painful. Later, after all, moved by the maternal nature, after her son looked for her and was injured, she still returned home to live a life of happiness in suffering.

As far as the actors are concerned, no one is working hard. Not only is the protagonist effective, but none of the supporting roles are mismatched. It is true that everyone is suitable for their own identity and personality. Of course, this is the joint effort of the director and the actors to achieve this perfect result. Especially the child star Li Keng, how touching his expression is, and even gives the audience a deep impression.

In terms of subtitles, many places use especially clever and humorous language. You only need to carefully savor it to know its magic. At the same time, it also uses symbolic and audible expressions, which can be said to be meticulous.

After the first act, the last act follows closely, recalling her life in the nunnery. This kind of editing is special and is the first of its kind in Chinese films.

In this film, the knocking of the wooden fish and the blacksmithing in (Life) I think have the same effect.

(Life) has already had considerable honor in society. I can predict that this film will certainly not fall behind (Life), maybe it will be ahead of (Life), because it is much more advanced than (Life)! (Respectful Reward)

Film Novel

Long Live Freedom (Viva Villa) (7) 251

— Wen Ying

Ban Zhuo was instructing Sykes on how to write news for him, but Ferro suddenly refused. He said... "Wait a minute, I am the mastermind. You write my name in it." Ban Zhuo scolded angrily... "Get out! You don't need to care about him. You write about me first." Ferro heard this, pulled out his gun, pointed at Sykes and said... "You obediently write my name in it"! Ban Zhuo also pulled out his gun and roared... "Do Americans need to know what Ferro did? Bastard." Ferro shouted loudly... "Who killed the chief judge and his friend? It was me!" Ban Zhuo said... "What does that matter. Without my order?" Sykes persuaded while afraid, pushing the muzzles of the two bandit leaders away from his head. Just as they were arguing and unable to resolve it, a bandit ran in like a whirlwind and shouted... "Ban Zhuo! Go quickly! The two brigades have already arrived! Hurry!" Ban Zhuo quickly walked to the door, looked around, and saw that a brigade of cavalry had already arrived in the town. His men had all jumped on their horses, firing their guns randomly, hitting the glass windows on both sides of the street, and then whipping their horses and fleeing. Ban Zhuo turned his head and shouted at Sykes... "Let's go! Come with me!" Sykes said... "No, I still have to send a telegram." Ban Zhuo said... "It doesn't matter, we can find another telegraph office." Sykes still refused to go. But Ban Zhuo pulled him to the door, gently embraced him, put him on the horse and galloped away.

Ban Zhuo had only gone a short distance when he saw a photography studio by the roadside with the words "Gavedo Special Photography" written on the signboard. Ban Zhuo saw it, reined in his horse, and jumped down. Ferro was so frightened that he asked him what he was doing. He said I want to see a friend, an artist. Sykes said... "They are all catching up." Ban Zhuo said... "It doesn't matter." He took Ferro, Thomas and Sykes and a group of people and walked into the photography studio. Gavado was a small man. When he saw Ban Zhuo, he shouted... "Hey, Ban Zhuo, do you still have time to take pictures now?" Ban Zhuo said... "I don't want to take pictures. I want you to write a letter for me. Do you know that woman called Sister Lucy? I want to marry her as my wife. You write a letter for me, saying that I will go to her tonight." Sykes said in surprise... "Are you getting married?" Ferro interjected... "He likes to get married the most. He gets married every two or three days." Ban Zhuo said... "I am like this by nature, almost religious. Gavado, you tell Lucida that I am going to her house tonight, around eleven o'clock. Tell her to prepare. Everything should be good." Gavado started writing the letter. As he wrote, he read... "My glorious queen... my little dove..." Ferro was standing by the window, watching the central army cavalry pass by. He took out his gun and muttered... "I can hit three of them at once." Sykes quickly shouted at him not to shoot. At this time, Gavado's letter was almost written, and Ban Zhuo still wanted him to draw something nice on the letter. Gavado said... "Okay. What do you like to draw? Two doves kissing each other?" Ban Zhuo said... "I think doves are not good. Draw something like me. A cow." Gavado said... "No, no. It's not good to draw that thing on a letter. I'll draw a heart for you, pierced by an arrow..." Ban Zhuo said... "No. You draw a cow for me. You listen to me." Gavado refused. Ban Zhuo grabbed him and pointed at him fiercely and said... "Will you draw it or not?" Gavado shouted... "You can kill me. I just won't draw a cow! I won't draw a cow"! Ban Zhuo really took out his gun. He gritted his teeth and said... "I order you! You draw a cow for me"! Gavado had no choice but to agree. But when he finished drawing, Ban Zhuo picked up the paper and looked at it, and it was still two doves kissing each other. Ban Zhuo wanted to raise his gun and fire, but Sykes stopped him. At this time, the central army had surrounded the place, Ban Zhuo said to Gavado... "Gavado, you come with us. I like art the most." As he said this, he tied up Gavado in the same way he tied up Sykes. (To be continued)
